The First Objection: Divine Action and Rarefaction Avoid Void
Opponent presents two ways to avoid void: divine action or rarefaction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two variants of the first objection to the void proof: the appeal to divine creation/annihilation and the appeal to rarefaction/condensation of bodies.

Core Idea
Void can be avoided by divine intervention or physical change.

The opponent attempts to block the void proof by offering two plausible mechanisms: either God creates a body in the space vacated and annihilates one in the target space, or the moving body itself rarefies and condenses to adjust volumes. Both appear to eliminate any need for void.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice that the opponent presents two distinct ways to avoid void.
The passage states these are 'not far-fetched'.
2
Identify the two variants
The first variant invokes divine action (الفاعل المختار) creating and annihilating parts. The second uses natural rarefaction and condensation (التخلخل والتكاثف). Note how each eliminates void.
3
Reflect on the intended goal
The opponent's goal is to show that the earlier proof for void is not necessary. Ask yourself: Do these objections seem convincing at first glance?
The commentary will later reveal a logical flaw.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : إن الجسم إذا انتقل من جانب إلى جانب ، فإنه يحدث في الحيز المنتقل عنه جسم ويعدم عن الحيز المنتقل إليه آخر و حينئذ لا يحصل الخلاء. ويفنى من الجانب المنتقل إليه جزء ، ليصير ذلك الحيز حيزاً لهذا المنتقل وحينئذ لا يلزم القول بالخلاء وهذا الذي ذكرناه غير مستبعد البتة إما لأجل أنا نقول : بالفاعل المختار فإنه تعالى يحدث جزءاً في أحد الحيزين ، ويفنى جزءاً عن الحيز الآخر وعلى هذا التقدير فالأشكال زائل لأجل أنا نقول : الأجسام قابلة للتخلخل والتكاثف ، فإذا انتقل الجسم عن حيز ، ازداد مقدار الجسم في الجانب المنتقل عنه ، وانتقص مقداره في الجانب المنتقل إليه ، وعلى التقديرين فالمقصود حاصل ثم نقول : هذا الدليل ينتقض بحركة السمكة في الماء ، فإنه لا يعقل حصول الخلاء في داخل الماء وذلك لأن الماء جرم سيال بالطبع إلى المواضع الخالية . فلو حصل هناك خلاء ، لسال الماء إليه . فيثبت : أنه ليس في داخل الماء شيء من الخلاء ، وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : إن السمكة إذا تحركت في قعر البحر ، لزمكم أن تقولوا : إنه يتموج بكليته ويتدافع بسبب حركة تلك السمكة فإن التزمتم ذلك ، فنحن أيضاً نلتزم تدافع أجزاء العالم بسبب حركة البقة . والجواب عن الأول : أن نقول : صحة إحداث الله الجسم في الحيز المنتقل عنه : مشروط بكون ذلك الحيز خالياً . لامتناع تداخل الأجسام ، فلو جعلنا صحة خلوه مشروطاً بخلق الله تعالى ذلك الجزء فيه ، لزم الدور ، وهو باطل وكذا القول في إعدام الحيز عن الجانب المنتقل إليه ، لأن هذا الإعدام مشروط بعدم الخلاء ، وعدم الخلاء مشروط بحصول الجسم المنتقل في ذلك الحيز ، فلو جعلنا صحة حصوله فيه مشروطاً بإعدام ذلك الحيز ، لزم الدور وهذا الجواب لا يختلف سواء قلنا : إنه يحدث أحد الجسمين ويعدم الآخر بإيجاد الله تعالى وبإعدامه ، أو قلنا : إنه يزداد مقدار الجسم من أحد الجانبين، وينتقص من الجانب الآخر بسبب التخلخل والتكاثف على أنا قد بينا
Then it is said: Why is it not permissible to say that when a body transfers from one side to another, then it brings into existence in the space transferred from a body and annihilates from the space transferred to another [body], and then no void occurs? And it annihilates from the side transferred to a part, so that that space becomes a space for this transferring thing, and then the statement of void does not follow. And this which we have mentioned is not far-fetched at all, either because we say: by the free agent, for He, exalted, brings into existence a part in one of the two spaces and annihilates a part from the other space. On this estimation, the difficulty is removed, because we say: bodies are susceptible to rarefaction and condensation, so when the body transfers from a space, the amount of the body increases on the side transferred from and decreases its amount on the side transferred to. On both estimations, the intended [result] is obtained. Then we say: This proof is undermined by the movement of a fish in water, for the occurrence of void within water is inconceivable, because water is a fluid body by nature flowing to empty places. So if there were void there, water would flow to it. So it is established that there is no void inside water. And when this is established, we say: If the fish moves at the bottom of the sea, you would be compelled to say that it undulates in its entirety and is pushed due to the movement of that fish. So if you commit to that, we also commit to the pushing of the parts of the world due to the movement of a flea. And the answer to the first: We say: The validity of God's bringing into existence the body in the space transferred from is conditioned by that space being void, due to the impossibility of interpenetration of bodies. So if we make the validity of its being void conditioned by God's creation of that part in it, circularity would follow, and it is false. And likewise the statement regarding the annihilation of the space from the side transferred to, because this annihilation is conditioned by the absence of void, and the absence of void is conditioned by the occurrence of the transferring body in that space. So if we make the validity of its occurrence in it conditioned by the annihilation of that space, circularity would follow. And this answer does not differ whether we say: He brings into existence one of the two bodies and annihilates the other by God's bringing into existence and His annihilation, or we say: the amount of the body increases on one side and decreases on the other due to rarefaction and condensation, given that we have shown...
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage contains two objections and the start of an answer to the first objection. The first objection proposes that void can be avoided by divine action: when a body moves, God creates a body in the vacated space and annihilates a part in the target space, so no void occurs. Alternatively, rarefaction and condensation of bodies could adjust the amounts without void. The second objection uses the example of a fish in water: water is fluid and fills any void immediately, so motion in water does not require void; thus the condition of void for motion is not universal, and the earlier proof is undermined. The author then begins answering the first objection by pointing out a circularity: for God to create a body in the vacated space, that space must already be void (since bodies cannot interpenetrate); but if its voidness is made conditional on creation, it is circular. Similarly, annihilation in the target space requires the absence of void, which in turn requires the moving body's presence, leading to another circle. The answer concludes that the same circularity applies whether one posits creation/annihilation or rarefaction/condensation. The answer to the second objection is not provided in this passage.

Key Terms
الفاعل المختار (the free agent)
التخلخل والتكاثف (rarefaction and condensation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objections are clearly invalid because they rely on miracles or are far-fetched.
Correction: The opponent explicitly states these are not far-fetched; the debate takes them seriously as plausible challenges.

Checkpoint
How many variants does the opponent give to avoid void?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
The first objection proposes two ways to avoid void: divine intervention or physical rarefaction, and these are taken seriously as plausible challenges to the void proof.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a difficult theological question, do you tend to appeal to 'God's power' as a quick answer? This passage shows that even appealing to divine action must be logically consistent. In what area of your faith have you used a shortcut instead of seeking deeper understanding? Will you commit to studying that issue thoroughly, even if it challenges you?
?
The opponent in this passage relies on natural processes (rarefaction/condensation) to avoid a logical problem. Are there areas in your life where you rely on 'how things naturally are' to avoid facing the reality of Allah's constant involvement? Examine one habit you do automatically—do you remember that Allah is the one creating that action each moment?
?
The passage takes the opponent's objection seriously and responds. Is there an objection to your own beliefs that you have dismissed without honest consideration? This week, write down one objection you fear, and seek to understand it from the source, just as the scholars did. Will you do that, even if it makes you uncomfortable?

The Second Objection: The Fish in Water Undermines the Void Proof
Opponent uses fish movement to show motion without void.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second objection using the fish in water to challenge the necessity of void for motion.

Core Idea
A fish moves in water without creating void, disproving a universal need for void.

The opponent presents a concrete counterexample: a fish swimming in water. Water is fluid and immediately fills any empty space, so no void occurs. If the void proof were correct, the entire sea would have to undulate absurdly with every fish movement, which is not observed.

Guided Path
1
Read the fish example
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the opponent's claim that void does not occur inside water.
Water is described as a fluid body (جرم سيال).
2
Understand the reasoning
The opponent argues that water flows to empty places, so if void appeared, water would fill it immediately. Therefore, void cannot exist inside water.
3
Grasp the reductio ad absurdum
If the void proof were true, then a fish moving would require void and thus the entire sea would undulate. The opponent says this is absurd, and if you accept it, then we could claim the world undulates due to a flea's movement.
This is a rhetorical reduction to show the proof's flaw.

Answering the First Objection: Exposing the Circularity
Author refutes first objection by exposing circularity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the circularity argument that refutes the first objection's two variants.

Core Idea
The first objection fails because it leads to a logical circle.

The author begins answering the first objection by identifying a vicious circularity in both variants. Whether one posits divine creation/annihilation or rarefaction/condensation, the conditions required lead to a logical dependency that loops back on itself. This demonstrates the impossibility of the opponent's escapes.

Guided Path
1
Read the answer carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation. The answer is structured as a conditional argument showing circularity (دور).
Look for the phrase 'لزم الدور' (circularity would follow).
2
Identify the first circle
For creation: the validity of creating a body in the vacated space requires that space to be void. But the voidness is made conditional on creation. This is circular.
3
Identify the second circle
For annihilation: the annihilation of a part in the target space requires the absence of void, which in turn requires the moving body to be present there. But the body's presence is made conditional on annihilation. Circular.
4
Note the generality of the answer
The author states that the same circularity applies whether one uses divine action (creation/annihilation) or rarefaction/condensation.
This shows the answer defeats both variants.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : إن الجسم إذا انتقل من جانب إلى جانب ، فإنه يحدث في الحيز المنتقل عنه جسم ويعدم عن الحيز المنتقل إليه آخر و حينئذ لا يحصل الخلاء. ويفنى من الجانب المنتقل إليه جزء ، ليصير ذلك الحيز حيزاً لهذا المنتقل وحينئذ لا يلزم القول بالخلاء وهذا الذي ذكرناه غير مستبعد البتة إما لأجل أنا نقول : بالفاعل المختار فإنه تعالى يحدث جزءاً في أحد الحيزين ، ويفنى جزءاً عن الحيز الآخر وعلى هذا التقدير فالأشكال زائل لأجل أنا نقول : الأجسام قابلة للتخلخل والتكاثف ، فإذا انتقل الجسم عن حيز ، ازداد مقدار الجسم في الجانب المنتقل عنه ، وانتقص مقداره في الجانب المنتقل إليه ، وعلى التقديرين فالمقصود حاصل ثم نقول : هذا الدليل ينتقض بحركة السمكة في الماء ، فإنه لا يعقل حصول الخلاء في داخل الماء وذلك لأن الماء جرم سيال بالطبع إلى المواضع الخالية . فلو حصل هناك خلاء ، لسال الماء إليه . فيثبت : أنه ليس في داخل الماء شيء من الخلاء ، وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : إن السمكة إذا تحركت في قعر البحر ، لزمكم أن تقولوا : إنه يتموج بكليته ويتدافع بسبب حركة تلك السمكة فإن التزمتم ذلك ، فنحن أيضاً نلتزم تدافع أجزاء العالم بسبب حركة البقة . والجواب عن الأول : أن نقول : صحة إحداث الله الجسم في الحيز المنتقل عنه : مشروط بكون ذلك الحيز خالياً . لامتناع تداخل الأجسام ، فلو جعلنا صحة خلوه مشروطاً بخلق الله تعالى ذلك الجزء فيه ، لزم الدور ، وهو باطل وكذا القول في إعدام الحيز عن الجانب المنتقل إليه ، لأن هذا الإعدام مشروط بعدم الخلاء ، وعدم الخلاء مشروط بحصول الجسم المنتقل في ذلك الحيز ، فلو جعلنا صحة حصوله فيه مشروطاً بإعدام ذلك الحيز ، لزم الدور وهذا الجواب لا يختلف سواء قلنا : إنه يحدث أحد الجسمين ويعدم الآخر بإيجاد الله تعالى وبإعدامه ، أو قلنا : إنه يزداد مقدار الجسم من أحد الجانبين، وينتقص من الجانب الآخر بسبب التخلخل والتكاثف على أنا قد بينا
Then it is said: Why is it not permissible to say that when a body transfers from one side to another, then it brings into existence in the space transferred from a body and annihilates from the space transferred to another [body], and then no void occurs? And it annihilates from the side transferred to a part, so that that space becomes a space for this transferring thing, and then the statement of void does not follow. And this which we have mentioned is not far-fetched at all, either because we say: by the free agent, for He, exalted, brings into existence a part in one of the two spaces and annihilates a part from the other space. On this estimation, the difficulty is removed, because we say: bodies are susceptible to rarefaction and condensation, so when the body transfers from a space, the amount of the body increases on the side transferred from and decreases its amount on the side transferred to. On both estimations, the intended [result] is obtained. Then we say: This proof is undermined by the movement of a fish in water, for the occurrence of void within water is inconceivable, because water is a fluid body by nature flowing to empty places. So if there were void there, water would flow to it. So it is established that there is no void inside water. And when this is established, we say: If the fish moves at the bottom of the sea, you would be compelled to say that it undulates in its entirety and is pushed due to the movement of that fish. So if you commit to that, we also commit to the pushing of the parts of the world due to the movement of a flea. And the answer to the first: We say: The validity of God's bringing into existence the body in the space transferred from is conditioned by that space being void, due to the impossibility of interpenetration of bodies. So if we make the validity of its being void conditioned by God's creation of that part in it, circularity would follow, and it is false. And likewise the statement regarding the annihilation of the space from the side transferred to, because this annihilation is conditioned by the absence of void, and the absence of void is conditioned by the occurrence of the transferring body in that space. So if we make the validity of its occurrence in it conditioned by the annihilation of that space, circularity would follow. And this answer does not differ whether we say: He brings into existence one of the two bodies and annihilates the other by God's bringing into existence and His annihilation, or we say: the amount of the body increases on one side and decreases on the other due to rarefaction and condensation, given that we have shown...
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage contains two objections and the start of an answer to the first objection. The first objection proposes that void can be avoided by divine action: when a body moves, God creates a body in the vacated space and annihilates a part in the target space, so no void occurs. Alternatively, rarefaction and condensation of bodies could adjust the amounts without void. The second objection uses the example of a fish in water: water is fluid and fills any void immediately, so motion in water does not require void; thus the condition of void for motion is not universal, and the earlier proof is undermined. The author then begins answering the first objection by pointing out a circularity: for God to create a body in the vacated space, that space must already be void (since bodies cannot interpenetrate); but if its voidness is made conditional on creation, it is circular. Similarly, annihilation in the target space requires the absence of void, which in turn requires the moving body's presence, leading to another circle. The answer concludes that the same circularity applies whether one posits creation/annihilation or rarefaction/condensation. The answer to the second objection is not provided in this passage.

Key Terms
الدور (circularity)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Divine action or rarefaction are perfect explanations that avoid circularity.
Correction: The argument shows they lead to a vicious circle; the conditions cannot be satisfied without circular dependency.

Checkpoint
What logical problem does the author identify in the first objection?
A) Infinite regress
B) Circularity (دور)
C) Contradiction with divine attributes
D) Empirical falsification

Key Takeaway
The first objection is refuted by exposing a logical circle: the conditions required for creation and annihilation depend on each other, making the proposal impossible.

The Main Proof for Vacuum
Razi presents a logical proof for vacuum via body movement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's logical proof that vacuum necessarily exists when a body moves from the side to the center of a small surface with no openings.

Core Idea
Vacuum is logically necessary: a body cannot be in two places at once.

Razi begins by setting up a simple physical scenario: a small surface with no openings. He then reasons that when a body moves from the side to the center, either it passes through the edge (impossible) or its passage is considered. This leads to a critical disjunction: the body cannot be both at the edge and the center simultaneously, so the center must have been empty—proving vacuum.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
Razi imagines a small surface with no openings. A body moves from the side to the center. The surface is raised all at once.
This is a thought experiment, not a real physical setup.
2
Follow the logical disjunctions
The body's movement is analyzed: either it passes through the edge (clearly invalid) or its passage is considered in another way. Then, either the body is at both the edge and center at once (impossible) or only at the edge.
The argument uses a series of 'either/or' statements to narrow possibilities.
3
Recognize the impossibility of dual occupation
A single body cannot occupy two places simultaneously. This is a fundamental principle.
This principle is used to eliminate one option.
4
Conclude the existence of vacuum
If the body is only at the edge, then when it was at the edge, the center was empty. This is the desired conclusion.
The proof is complete: vacuum must exist at that moment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المتصلة، قد ارتفع عنا تحته دفعة واحدة فإذا لم يكن في ذلك السطح الصغير شيء من المنافد امتنع أن يقال : الجسم دخل في منافده، والثاني أيضاً باطل. لأن انتقال تلك الأجسام من الجوانب إلى الوسط، إما أن يعتبر فيها مرورها بالطرف، وهو ظاهر الفساد، أو يعتبر فيه ذلك . وحينئذ لا يخلو إما أن يقال إنه : حين يكون في الطرف يكون في الوسط أيضاً، وهو ممتنع . لأن الجسم الواحد لا يحصل دفعة واحدة في حيزين، أو يقال : إنه حين يكون حاصلاً في الطرف، لا يكون حاصلاً في الوسط . وحينئذ يلزم أن يقال : إن حين كان ذلك الجسم حاصلاً في الطرف، كان الوسط خالياً . وهو المطلوب . فإن قيل : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : إنه كلما ارتفع أحد السطحين عن الآخر، فإن الفاعل المختار يخلق في ذلك الوسط جسماً . وحينئذ لا يلزم القول بالخلاء ؟ أو يقال : إنه كلما ارتفع أحد السطحين عن الآخر فإن الأجسام المحيطة بهما تتخلخل ويزداد عظمها، ويمتلىء الوسط بها في الحال ؟ والجواب . أما الأول فمدفوع من وجهين : الأول : إن الفاعل المختار لا يقول به الفلاسفة . والثاني : يلزم الدور المذكور، وذلك لأن صحة إحداث الجسم هناك، مشروط بارتفاع أحد ذينك السطحين عن الآخر، لئلا يلزم تداخل الأجسام، فلو جعلنا صحة ارتفاع أحد ذينك السطحين عن الآخر مشروطة بإحداث ذلك الجسم، لزم الدور. وأما القول بازدياد مقادير الأجسام المحيطة بدينك السطحين فهو باطل . لوجهين : الأول : هذا المذهب باطل على ما بيناه في باب الحركة والثاني : هو أنا نقول : هب أن هذا الازدياد ممكن، إلا أن طرف ذلك الجسم المتخلخل، لا بد وأن يمتد من الخارج إلى الداخل، فحين يكون طرفه متصلاً بطرف ذينك السطحين، يكون الوسط خالياً عنه، وحينئذ يحصل المطلوب والله أعلم.
The connected [surface] has been raised from us beneath it all at once. If there is no opening in that small surface, it is impossible to say: the body entered through its openings. The second [alternative] is also false. Because the transition of those bodies from the sides to the center, either its passage by the edge is considered, which is manifestly invalid, or that is considered in it. Then it is inevitable either to say: when it is at the edge it is also in the center, which is impossible because one body cannot occupy two places at once, or to say: when it is present at the edge, it is not present in the center. Then it necessarily follows to say: when that body was present at the edge, the center was empty. That is the desired conclusion. If it is said: Why is it not permissible to say that whenever one of the two surfaces is raised from the other, the free agent (al-fāʿil al-mukhtār) creates a body in that center, and then the assertion of vacuum does not follow? Or is it said: Whenever one of the two surfaces is raised from the other, the bodies surrounding them expand and their size increases, and the center is filled with them instantly? The answer: As for the first [objection], it is refuted from two aspects: First: The philosophers do not affirm the free agent. Second: The mentioned circularity follows, because the validity of creating a body there is conditioned by the raising of one of those two surfaces from the other, lest interpenetration of bodies occur. If we made the validity of raising one of the two surfaces from the other conditioned by the creation of that body, circularity would follow. As for the assertion of the increase in the magnitudes of the bodies surrounding those two surfaces, it is false for two aspects: First: This doctrine is false according to what we explained in the chapter on motion. Second: We say: Suppose this increase is possible, but the extremity of that rarefied body must extend from outside to inside. When its extremity is connected to the extremity of those two surfaces, the center is empty of it, and then the desired conclusion obtains. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage presents a proof for the existence of vacuum (al-khalā') by analyzing the movement of bodies across a small surface. The author begins by assuming a small surface with no openings. If a body moves from the side to the center, either it passes through the edge (invalid) or its passage is considered. Then either the body is simultaneously at the edge and center (impossible, as one body cannot occupy two places) or it is at the edge but not in the center, which implies the center was empty—the desired conclusion. Two objections are raised: (1) A free agent could create a body in the center as the surfaces separate, avoiding vacuum. (2) The surrounding bodies could expand to fill the gap. The answer to the first objection is twofold: philosophers deny the free agent, and circularity arises because the raising of surfaces is conditioned on the creation of a body to avoid interpenetration, but if creation is conditioned on raising, it becomes circular. The second objection is false because expansion would require the body's extremity to extend inward, and at the moment of connection with the surfaces, the center is still empty. The argument follows a logical structure: presenting the main proof, then addressing counterarguments in order, using reduction to impossibility and circularity.

Key Terms
الخلاء (al-khalā')
الجسم (al-jism)
السطح (al-sath)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Razi conclude that the center must be empty?
A) Because the body is too large to fit.
B) Because the body cannot be at the edge and center simultaneously.
C) Because the surface has no openings.
D) Because the body moves slowly.

Key Takeaway
The logical impossibility of a body being in two places at once forces the conclusion that vacuum must exist in the described scenario.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Razi uses logical reasoning to prove something invisible—vacuum. What is one area of your faith where you rely on logical proofs but struggle to feel the reality? What step can you take today to bridge that gap between intellectual assent and heartfelt conviction?
?
The proof eliminates alternatives until only one truth remains. In your life, what false alternatives have you been holding onto—perhaps in your habits, relationships, or priorities—that you know are impossible when examined in light of divine truth? What would it cost you to let them go and embrace the logical conclusion?

Objections and Responses to the Vacuum Proof
Razi refutes two objections to his vacuum proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main objections to Razi's vacuum proof and his rebuttals, including the problem of circularity.

Core Idea
Objections to vacuum fail due to circularity or logical gaps.

After presenting his proof, Razi anticipates two objections: one involving a free agent creating a body to fill the gap, and another suggesting that surrounding bodies expand to fill the space. He refutes both, showing that the first leads to circular reasoning and the second still leaves a moment of emptiness before expansion is complete.

Guided Path
1
Understand the first objection
Objector: The free agent (God) could create a body in the center as the surfaces separate, preventing vacuum.
This objection assumes a creator who can intervene.
2
Analyze the response to the first objection
Razi gives two rebuttals: (a) philosophers do not affirm a free agent, and (b) it leads to circularity—the creation of a body depends on the separation of surfaces, but separation is made dependent on creation.
The circularity is a logical flaw: each step presupposes the other.
3
Understand the second objection
Objector: The surrounding bodies could expand (rarefy) to fill the center instantly.
This avoids vacuum by continuous expansion.
4
Analyze the response to the second objection
Razi says this view is false per his earlier work on motion. But even if possible, the extremity of the expanding body extends inward, and when it first touches the surfaces, the center is still empty before being filled.
So vacuum is not avoided; it merely precedes the filling.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

?

?
Razi points out that even if expansion were possible, a moment of emptiness remains. What 'empty' areas in your spiritual life have you been trying to fill with distractions rather than facing the void? Will you honestly acknowledge them today?

Fifth Proof: The Waterskin Experiment
Razi presents the waterskin argument to demonstrate the existence of internal vacuum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses the waterskin experiment to argue for the existence of vacuum and how he refutes one objection by appealing to empirical necessity.

Core Idea
If you can insert a needle into a fully inflated waterskin, there must be empty space inside.

Razi presents a physical experiment involving a waterskin and needles to prove the existence of internal vacuum. He then anticipates and responds to possible objections. This lesson walks through the argument, the three objections, and the refutation of the first, showing how empirical observation can settle a theoretical dispute.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: the claim, the experimental setup, the conclusion, and then the objections and answer.
The proof relies on the impossibility of interpenetration of bodies if no vacuum exists.
2
Identify the three objections
Find the three alternative explanations the author considers: expansion of the waterskin, escape of air through pores, and condensation of the internal air.
Each objection tries to explain the needle's entry without vacuum.
3
Examine the answer to the first objection
Notice how Razi refutes the expansion objection by appealing to the amount of force required. He argues that maximal expansion would require great force, but needle insertion is easy, so expansion cannot explain it.
This refutation uses empirical necessity ('ilm bi al-ḍarūra).

الحجة الخامسة : إن الإنسان قد ينفخ في الزق نفحاً شديداً بحيث لا يمكنه أن يزيد على ذلك النفخ، ثم يسد رأس ذلك الزق سداً وثيقاً، ثم إنه بعد ذلك لو حاول غرز المسلة الواحدة فيه أو الأعداد الكثيرة من المسلات في ذلك الزق، أمكنه ذلك . ولولا أنه حصل في داخل ذلك الزق المنفوخ خلاء كثير، وإلا لما أمكن ذلك، لأنه يلزم تداخل الاجسام . فإن قيل : لعل المسلة إنما نفدت في ذلك الزق لان عند حصول ذلك الغرز، يتمدد جرم الزق ويتسع، فيحصل لتلك المسلة مكان في داخل ذلك الزق المنفوخ، أو يقال : لعله حصل عند غرز المسلة في الزق، خروج بعض أجزاء الهواء المنفوخ فيه من مسام ذلك الزق. وحينئذ يتسع داخل ذلك الزق لنفود المسلة فيه . أو يقال : ثبت أن الأجسام قابلة للتخلخل والتكاثف، فلعل عند غرز المسلة تكاثق ذلك الهواء المنفوخ في الزق وانقبض، فحصل للمسلة المغروزة في ذلك الداخل مكان. وإذا كانت هذه الاحتمالات قائمة امتنع الاستدلال، بإمكان غرز المسلة في الزق المنفوخ على حصول الخلاء داخل ذلك الزق والجواب عن الأول. إنا نفرض الكلام فيما إذا بالغ الإنسان في تمديد الزق، قبل أن ينفخ فيه، ثم بالغ في النفخ مبالغة لا يمكنه أن يزيد عليها . فههنا لا شك أن أجزاء الزق قد تمددت بسبب المبالغة في التمديد أولاً، والنفخ ثانياً . فلو حصل بسبب غرز المسلة فيه تمدد أزيد مما كان، لما حصل ذلك إلا بعد قوة شديدة وتكلف عظيم. لكنا نعلم بالضرورة أنه لا يحتاج في هذا الغرز إلى قوة شديدة، فبطل هذا الاحتمال .
The fifth proof: A person may blow into a waterskin (al-ziqq) a strong blow such that he cannot exceed that blow, then close the mouth of that waterskin tightly. Then after that, if he attempts to insert one needle (al-misallah) or many needles into that waterskin, he is able to do so. Were it not that much vacuum (khalā') occurred inside that blown-up waterskin, that would not be possible, because interpenetration of bodies would follow. If it is said: Perhaps the needle penetrates that waterskin because when that insertion occurs, the body of the waterskin expands and widens, and a place for that needle is obtained inside that blown-up waterskin. Or it is said: Perhaps when the needle is inserted into the waterskin, some parts of the air blown into it exit through the pores of that waterskin, and then the inside of that waterskin widens for the penetration of the needle into it. Or it is said: It is established that bodies are susceptible to rarefaction (takhalkhul) and condensation (takāthuf), so perhaps when the needle is inserted, that air blown into the waterskin condenses and contracts, and a place is obtained for the inserted needle in that interior. If these possibilities are present, the inference from the possibility of inserting the needle into the blown-up waterskin to the occurrence of vacuum inside that waterskin is prevented. The answer to the first [objection]: We consider the case when a person stretches the waterskin to the utmost before blowing into it, then blows into it with such intensity that he cannot increase it. Here there is no doubt that the parts of the waterskin have expanded due to the extreme stretching first and the blowing second. If, due to the insertion of the needle, further expansion occurred beyond what was, that would only happen with great force and extreme effort. But we know by necessity that this insertion does not require great force, so this possibility is invalidated.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth proof for the existence of vacuum, based on a physical experiment. The proof: A person blows into a waterskin as hard as possible, seals it, and then easily inserts one or many needles into it. If there were no void space inside, this would be impossible because it would require interpenetration of bodies. Therefore, vacuum exists inside. Three objections are raised: (1) The waterskin stretches further upon needle insertion, creating space. (2) Air escapes through pores, making room. (3) The air inside condenses, allowing the needle in. The author answers only the first objection, arguing that if the waterskin is already maximally stretched and blown, any additional expansion would require great force, but we know from immediate experience that inserting a needle requires little force; thus the expansion explanation is invalid. The argument proceeds by presenting the main proof, listing alternatives, and then refuting the first alternative by appealing to empirical necessity ('ilm bi al-ḍarūra). The other two objections are not addressed in this passage.

Key Terms
الزق (al-ziqq)
المسلة (al-misallah)
الخلاء (al-khalā')
تداخل الأجسام (tadākhul al-ajsām)
التخلخل (takhalkhul)
التكاثف (takāthuf)
الضرورة (al-ḍarūra)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All three objections are equally valid and undermine the proof entirely.
Correction: Razi refutes the first objection by showing it contradicts empirical necessity; the other two are not necessarily valid but are not answered here. The proof retains force after the refutation.

Checkpoint
What is the main reason Razi gives to refute the first objection (that the waterskin expands further when the needle is inserted)?
A) The waterskin cannot expand because it is already fully stretched.
B) If further expansion occurred, it would require great force, but we know inserting a needle requires little force.
C) The needle is too thin to cause expansion.
D) The experiment is not repeatable.

Key Takeaway
The waterskin experiment provides empirical evidence for vacuum, and the refutation of the first objection demonstrates how necessary knowledge ('ilm al-ḍarūra) can settle theoretical disputes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What 'theoretical possibilities' do you cling to in your own life to avoid accepting a simple truth that is evident from your own experience? Commit to identifying one such truth today and acting on it.
?
Just as the objections prevented admitting vacuum, do you invent excuses to avoid following a clear command of Allah? Write down one excuse you have used and then erase it, replacing it with a concrete step of obedience.
?
Think of a time when you knew something was true by necessity (like needing slight force) but entertained doubts anyway. What does this tell you about the condition of your heart? Resolve to trust your certain knowledge when it comes to matters of faith.

The Wineskin Experiment: Proof for Vacuum
Al-Razi presents and defends the fifth proof for vacuum via a wineskin experiment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's fifth proof for the existence of vacuum, the three objections raised against it, and how he systematically refutes each one.

Core Idea
A fully inflated wineskin still accepts needles — only vacuum can explain it.

This lesson examines a classic kalām argument for the existence of vacuum. Al-Razi uses a simple experiment with a wineskin and needles to demonstrate that empty space must exist within bodies. The argument is presented, then challenged with three objections, and each is systematically refuted. By following the logic, you will see how empirical observation is used to support a metaphysical conclusion about the nature of space.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument and experiment
Read the Arabic passage once. Then read the translation to understand the scenario: a wineskin is inflated as much as possible, sealed, and then needles are inserted easily. The conclusion is that vacuum must exist inside.
Notice that the proof relies on the impossibility of interpenetration of bodies.
2
Understand the first objection and its refutation
The first objection suggests the wineskin stretches further. Al-Razi answers that since the wineskin was already maximally stretched, any further stretching would require great force, but the insertion is easy, so the objection fails.
Pay attention to the condition of maximal stretching before inflation.
3
Understand the second objection and its refutation
The second objection claims air escapes through pores. Al-Razi counters that if air did not escape during intense blowing, it cannot escape during gentle insertion without great force, which is absent.
This refutation uses the same logic of requiring force.
4
Understand the third objection and its refutation
The third objection invokes condensation of air. Al-Razi rejects this by stating that the theory of condensation and rarefaction is false, as established earlier in his work.
This refutation is doctrinal; it relies on prior kalām arguments.
5
Synthesize the proof
Reflect on how the three refutations together defend the conclusion that vacuum exists. Each shows that the alternative explanations are impossible or would require disproportionate force.
Consider why this proof matters for kalām cosmology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة : إن الإنسان قد ينفخ في الزق نفحاً شديداً بحيث لا يمكنه أن يزيد على ذلك النفخ ، ثم يسد رأس ذلك الزق سداً وثيقاً ، ثم إنه بعد ذلك لو حاول غرز المسلة الواحدة فيه أو الأعداد الكثيرة من المسلات في ذلك الزق ، أمكنه ذلك . ولولا أنه حصل في داخل ذلك الزق المنفوخ خلاء كثير ، وإلا لما أمكن ذلك ، لأنه يلزم تداخل الاجسام . فإن قيل : لعل المسلة إنما نفدت في ذلك الزق لان عند حصول ذلك الغرز ، يتمدد جرم الزق ويتسع ، فيحصل لتلك المسلة مكان في داخل ذلك الزق المنفوخ ، أو يقال : لعله حصل عند غرز المسلة في الزق، خروج بعض أجزاء الهواء المنفوخ فيه من مسام ذلك الزق. وحينئذ يتسع داخل ذلك الزق لنفود المسلة فيه . أو يقال : ثبت أن الأجسام قابلة للتخلخل والتكاثف ، فلعل عند غرز المسلة تكاثق ذلك الهواء المنفوخ في الزق وانقبض ، فحصل للمسلة المغروزة في ذلك الداخل مكان. وإذا كانت هذه الاحتمالات قائمة امتنع الاستدلال ، بإمكان غرز المسلة في الزق المنفوخ على حصول الخلاء داخل ذلك الزق والجواب عن الأول. إنا نفرض الكلام فيما إذا بالغ الإنسان في تمديد الزق ، قبل أن ينفخ فيه ، ثم بالغ في النفخ مبالغة لا يمكنه أن يزيد عليها . فههنا لا شك أن أجزاء الزق قد تمددت بسبب المبالغة في التمديد أولاً ، والنفخ ثانياً . فلو حصل بسبب غرز المسلة فيه تمدد أزيد مما كان ، لما حصل ذلك إلا بعد قوة شديدة وتكلف عظيم. لكنا نعلم بالضرورة أنه لا يحتاج في هذا الغرز إلى قوة شديدة ، فبطل هذا الاحتمال . وأما قوله ثانياً : لعل عند غرز هذه المسلة ، خرج بعض أجزاء الهواء من مسام الزق فجوابه : أن تلك الأجزاء لما لم تخرج عند المبالغة الشديدة في النفخ ، وجب أن لا تخرج أيضاً عند هذا الغرز ، إلا عند القوة الشديدة في هذا الغرز . ومعلوم أن هذا الغرز مما لا يحتاج إلى هذه القوة الشديدة . فصار هذا الاحتمال مدفوعاً . وأما قوله ثالثاً : إن الهواء المحصور في داخل الزق المنفوخ ، لعله يصير متكاثفاً منقبضاً . فجوابه : أن القول بالتكاتف والتخلخل باطل على ما قررناه في باب الحركة والله أعلم .
The fifth proof: A person may blow into a wineskin with such intense blowing that he cannot increase upon that blowing, then he seals the mouth of that wineskin tightly. Then after that, if he tries to insert one needle or a great number of needles into that wineskin, he can do so. And were it not that much vacuum (khalā') occurred inside that inflated wineskin, it would not be possible, because it would necessitate the interpenetration (tadākhul) of bodies. If it is said: Perhaps the needle only penetrates into that wineskin because upon the occurrence of that insertion, the body of the wineskin stretches and expands, so a place for that needle occurs inside that inflated wineskin. Or it is said: Perhaps upon inserting the needle into the wineskin, some parts of the air blown into it exit through the pores of that wineskin, and then the interior of that wineskin expands for the passage of the needle into it. Or it is said: It is established that bodies are susceptible to rarefaction and condensation (takhalʾul wa-takāthuf), so perhaps upon inserting the needle, that air blown into the wineskin condenses and contracts, so a place for the inserted needle occurs in that interior. And if these possibilities exist, the inference from the possibility of inserting the needle into the inflated wineskin to the occurrence of vacuum inside that wineskin is prevented. The answer to the first: We posit the case when a person has maximally stretched the wineskin before blowing into it, then he blows with an intensity he cannot exceed. Now, there is no doubt that the parts of the wineskin have stretched due to maximal stretching first and blowing second. If, due to the insertion of the needle, an additional stretching beyond what existed were to occur, that would only happen after great force and extreme effort. But we know by necessity that this insertion does not require great force, so this possibility is nullified. As for the second objection: 'Perhaps upon inserting this needle, some parts of the air exit from the pores of the wineskin,' the answer: Those parts, since they did not exit during the intense blowing, must not exit during this insertion either, except with great force in this insertion. And it is known that this insertion does not require such great force. So this possibility is refuted. As for the third objection: 'Perhaps the air confined inside the inflated wineskin condenses and contracts,' the answer: The doctrine of condensation (takāthuf) and rarefaction (takhalʾul) is false according to what we established in the chapter on motion. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth proof for the existence of vacuum (khalā') by means of a physical experiment. The proof is structured as an argument followed by three objections and their refutations. The author, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, begins by stating the scenario: a person blows into a leather wineskin (ziqq) as forcefully as possible, then seals it tightly. Despite being fully inflated, one can easily insert numerous needles into it. If the wineskin were completely filled with air, inserting a needle would require either the interpenetration of bodies (tadākhul al-ajsām), which is impossible, or the displacement of air. Since the insertion happens without difficulty, the only explanation is that there is empty space (vacuum) inside the wineskin into which the needle enters. The author then presents three objections and answers them in order. First objection: The wineskin stretches further upon insertion, creating space. Answer: The wineskin was already maximally stretched before blowing and during blowing; any further stretching would require great force, but the insertion is easy, so this is false. Second objection: Air escapes through pores, making room. Answer: Since the air did not escape even under the intense internal pressure during blowing, it would not escape during insertion unless great force is applied; yet the insertion is easy, so this is impossible. Third objection: The air inside condenses (becomes denser) upon insertion, making room. Answer: The theory of condensation and rarefaction (takāthuf wa-takhalʾul) is false, as already established in the chapter on motion—a reference to a prior argument that bodies cannot change density. Thus the proof for vacuum stands. The passage ends with 'And God knows best.' This argument is typical of kalām cosmology, using empirical observation to support metaphysical conclusions about the nature of space.

Key Terms
الخلاء
الزق
المسلة
تداخل الاجسام
التخلخل والتكاثف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The wineskin experiment is only about physical pressure and does not prove anything metaphysical about vacuum.
Correction: Al-Razi's argument is metaphysical: it aims to establish vacuum as a real entity, which is necessary for certain kalām doctrines about God's creative power and the nature of bodies.

Checkpoint
What is the main conclusion drawn from the experiment of inserting needles into an inflated wineskin?
A) Air is compressible under pressure.
B) Bodies can interpenetrate without harm.
C) There must be empty space (vacuum) inside the wineskin.
D) The wineskin stretches infinitely.

Key Takeaway
Through the wineskin experiment, al-Razi argues that vacuum must exist because only empty space can explain why needles enter without resistance, and all alternative explanations are refuted.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Razi proves something invisible (vacuum) through visible evidence and reason. What invisible realities have you accepted based on rational proof alone—and which ones have you resisted because you demand physical evidence? Will you trust your intellect when it leads you to truths you cannot see, including those about your Creator?
?
The objectors offered plausible alternatives (stretching, escaping air) that had to be refuted point by point. Are there plausible-sounding doubts about your faith—perhaps from modern science or culture—that you have left unrefuted? What would it take for you to confront them with the same rigorous reasoning al-Razi applies?
?
If a simple physical experiment like this required such careful reasoning to arrive at the truth, how much more care is needed when contemplating matters of the afterlife and divine will? Are you willing to engage in deep study to protect your creed, or are you content with superficial knowledge that may be shaken?

Refuting Objections on Air in the Waterskin
Razi refutes two objections about air in a punctured waterskin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Fakhr al-Din al-Razi refutes two objections regarding the behavior of air in an inflated waterskin when pierced.

Core Idea
Air's behavior under force reveals causal patterns that invalidate skeptical objections.

In this passage, al-Razi engages with two objections raised against arguments about air and causality in a punctured waterskin. The objections claim that air might escape through pores or condense inside. Razi refutes each using logical reasoning and references to earlier principles.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage and Translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation to understand the flow of objections and answers.
Notice the concise style of Razi's refutation.
2
Analyze the Defense Against Porosity
Focus on the first objection and answer. Understand the force argument: if air did not exit during strong blowing, it cannot exit with a weaker needle prick.
This is a logical consistency argument.
3
Examine the Condensation Refutation
Look at the second objection and answer. Razi rejects the condensation possibility by appealing to a prior refutation of condensation and rarefaction.
This shows reliance on established principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قوله ثانياً : لعل عند غرز هذه المسلة ، خرج بعض أجزاء الهواء من مسام الزق فجوابه : أن تلك الأجزاء لما لم تخرج عند المبالغة الشديدة في النفخ ، وجب أن لا تخرج أيضاً عند هذا الغرز ، إلا عند القوة الشديدة في هذا الغرز . ومعلوم أن هذا الغرز مما لا يحتاج إلى هذه القوة الشديدة . فصار هذا الاحتمال مدفوعاً .
وأما قوله ثالثاً : إن الهواء المحصور في داخل الزق المنفوخ ، لعله يصير متكاثفاً منقبضاً . فجوابه : أن القول بالتكاتف والتخلخل باطل على ما قررناه في باب الحركة [ والله أعلم ] .
And as for his second statement: 'Perhaps when piercing this needle, some parts of the air exit from the pores of the waterskin.' The answer to it is: Since those parts did not exit during the intense effort in blowing, it must be that they also do not exit at this piercing, unless with great force in this piercing. And it is known that this piercing does not require this great force. So this possibility is repelled. And as for his third statement: 'The air confined inside the inflated waterskin perhaps becomes dense and contracted.' The answer to it is: The statement about condensation and rarefaction is invalid according to what we established in the chapter on motion [and God knows best].
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of two objections concerning the behavior of air in an inflated waterskin. Razi presents each objection followed by his answer.

First objection: The opponent claims that when a needle is pierced into the waterskin, some air escapes through its pores. Razi's answer: If air did not escape even with strong blowing (which would force air out), it certainly cannot escape from a simple needle prick, since the prick involves much less force. Thus the opponent's scenario is impossible.

Second objection: The opponent suggests that the air inside the waterskin might become condensed or contracted (instead of escaping). Razi's answer: The theory of condensation and rarefaction has already been refuted in the chapter on motion, so this suggestion is invalid. This is a summary reference to an earlier established argument.

Key Terms
غرز المسلة
مسام الزق
النفخ
التكاثف
التخلخل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Air can always escape through tiny openings if the object is porous.
Correction: Razi shows that if air did not escape with stronger force (blowing), it cannot escape with weaker force (needle prick).

Checkpoint
What is Razi's main reason for rejecting the claim that air exits the waterskin when pierced by a needle?
A) Air cannot exist in a waterskin at all.
B) The needle pierces the skin but the air condenses instead.
C) The air did not exit even with strong blowing, so it cannot exit with a weaker force.
D) The waterskin is made of a material that prevents air escape.

Key Takeaway
Razi uses logical consistency and prior refutations to reject objections about air behavior in a waterskin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How often do you accept weak excuses for your own failures that you would never accept from others? Razi applied the same standard of force to both cases. Will you commit to using the same measure of accountability for yourself as you do for others?
?
The second objection was dismissed because its premise had already been refuted. Is there a foundational belief in your life—about Allah, about yourself, about the world—that you hold without checking if it has already been proven false? What would it take for you to revisit it?
?
Razi's argument is simple yet decisive. When you are confronted with doubts about your faith, do you seek out deep, consistent answers, or do you settle for superficial responses? What is one doubt you have been avoiding because you fear the answer?

The Jar Experiment: Proof of Vacuum
Razi presents the jar proof and the rarefaction objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sixth proof for the existence of vacuum based on the jar experiment and the opponents' objection invoking rarefaction.

Core Idea
The jar experiment shows that if air could rarefy, water would not rise.

Razi presents a compelling empirical proof: after sucking a jar and inverting it over water, water rises inside. This indicates that sucking removed some air, creating a vacuum. However, opponents counter that air expands (rarefies) to fill the space, and then contracts when the jar is inverted, allowing water entry. In this lesson, we explore both the proof and this objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof
Read the first part where Razi states the jar experiment and deduces the existence of a vacuum.
2
Understand the objection
Read the opponents' response: they claim rarefaction instead of vacuum.
Note the terms 'takhalkhul' and 'takathtuf'.
3
Compare the two explanations
Compare the simplicity of the vacuum explanation with the complexity of the rarefaction theory.
This sets up Razi's refutations in subsequent lessons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة : إن القارورة قد تمص ، ثم تكب على الماء ، فيتصاعد الماء إليها ، ولو كانت بعد المص مملوءة كما كانت قبل ذلك المص ، لوجب أن لا يتصاعد الماء إليها بعد المص ، كما لا يتصاعد الماء إليها قبل المص . فإن قالوا : إن بسبب المص خرج بعض ما كان في القارورة من الهواء ، ثم ازداد حجم البقية ازدياداً امتلات القارورة منه، إلا أن ذلك الازدياد كان قسرياً ، حاصلاً بسبب المص ، فلما كبت القارورة على الماء ، زال القاسر فعاد ذلك الهواء إلى مقداره الطبيعي ، الذي كان حاصلاً أولاً فتصاعد الماء إلى داخل القارورة ، لأجل ضرورة الخلاء
قلنا هذا باطل من وجوه :
الأول : إن القول بالتخلخل والتكاثف باطل محال على ما قررناه .
والثاني : هب أن ذلك ممكن إلا أنا نقول : إن عند حصول هذا التخلخل لزم القول بحدوث الذات، وليس هذا عبارة عن حدوث الصفة فقط لأن الجسم إذا ازداد حجمه ومقداره . فكل جزء من أجزاء ذلك المنبسط المتخلخل فهو ذات قائمة بالنفس كسائر الأجزاء . وأيضاً : فجميع تلك الأجزاء المفترضة في ذلك الجسم متشابهة بالماهية والطبيعة والحقيقة ، فعند زوال القاسر ، أو التقلص والقبض كان ذلك إشارة إلى عدم بعض تلك الأجزاء دون البعض. وهذا باطل . لأن تلك الأجزاء لما كانت متساوية في تمام الماهية لم يكن عدم بعضها أولى من عدم الباقي فإما أن يفنى الكل وهو محال ، أو يبقى الكل ، وحينئذ يلزم أن تبقى القارورة مملوءة كما كانت وحينئذ يجب أن لا يتصاعد الماء إليها بعد المص كما كان لا يتصاعد الماء إليها قبل المص .
والوجه الثالث في دفع هذا السؤال : أن نقول : ذكر الشيخ الرئيس أن الهيولى ليس لها في حد ذاتها وحقيقتها : حجمية ولا مقدار فكانت نسبتها إلى جميع المقادير على السوية ، هذا كلامه
ونحن نقول : إذا كان الأمر كذلك امتنع أن يقال : إن بعض المقادير بالنسبة إلى تلك المادة ، طبيعي لها ، وبعضها قسرى لها . لأن نسبة جميع إليها على السوية . وإذا كان الأمر كذلك ، فهذه الحجمية الحاصلة عند المص وعند التخلخل تكون طبيعة لتلك المادة ، فوجب أن تبقى وأن لا تنتقص عند إكباب القارورة على الماء [ والله أعلم ]
The sixth proof: The jar is sucked, then inverted over water, and the water ascends into it. And if after sucking it were as full as it was before that sucking, then water would not ascend into it after sucking, just as water does not ascend into it before sucking. And if they say: 'Because of the sucking, some of the air that was in the jar exited, then the remainder increased in volume such that the jar became filled with it, except that this increase was forced, occurring due to the sucking; then when the jar was inverted over the water, the coercer ceased and that air returned to its natural quantity that existed initially, so the water ascended into the jar due to the necessity of the vacuum.' We say: This is invalid from several aspects: First: The statement about rarefaction and condensation is invalid and impossible according to what we established. Second: Suppose that is possible, but we say: When this rarefaction occurs, it necessitates the statement of the origination of the essence, and this is not the origination of the attribute alone, because when a body increases in its volume and magnitude, every part of that expanded rarefied part is an essence subsisting in itself like the other parts. Also, all those hypothetical parts in that body are similar in essence, nature, and reality; so when the coercer ceases, or contraction and constriction occur, that would indicate the non-existence of some of those parts without others. And this is invalid because those parts, since they are equal in complete essence, the non-existence of some is no more appropriate than the non-existence of the rest. So either the whole perishes, which is impossible, or the whole remains, and then it follows that the jar remains full as it was, and then water should not ascend into it after sucking just as water did not ascend into it before sucking. The third aspect in repelling this question: We say: The Chief Master (Ibn Sina) mentioned that prime matter has in its own essence and reality neither volume nor magnitude, so its relation to all magnitudes is equal. This is his statement. And we say: If the matter is so, it is impossible to say that some magnitudes are natural for that matter and others are forced for it, because the relation of all of them to it is equal. And if the matter is so, then this volume that occurs during sucking and rarefaction would be natural for that matter, so it must remain and not decrease when the jar is inverted over water. [And God knows best].
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is a full argumentative unit: Razi presents the sixth proof (the jar experiment), then considers an objection from opponents who invoke rarefaction, and refutes it through three distinct aspects.

The proof: When a jar is sucked and then inverted into water, water rises inside. If the jar were still full of air after sucking, water would not rise. Therefore, sucking must have removed some air, creating a vacuum that draws water.

The opponents' objection: They claim that sucking caused some air to leave, but the remaining air expanded (rarefied) to fill the jar; this expansion is forced. When the jar is placed on water, the coercing cause (suction) ceases, so the air contracts back to its natural volume, allowing water to enter to fill the space left by contraction — not a vacuum.

Razi's refutation in three aspects:

First aspect: The theory of rarefaction and condensation has already been proven false in earlier discussions.

Second aspect: Even if rarefaction were possible, it would involve the origination of new essences (not just attributes). Because if air expands, each new portion of expanded volume is a new substance (essence) subsisting by itself, like other parts. And all parts are identical in essence. When the coercer ceases, if some parts vanish while others remain, this would be arbitrary discrimination among identical essences, which is impossible. Therefore, either all parts perish (impossible) or all remain, meaning the jar stays full and water cannot rise.

Third aspect: Citing Ibn Sina (the 'Chief Master'), prime matter (hayula) in itself has no inherent volume or magnitude; it is equally related to all magnitudes. If so, no magnitude is 'natural' to it over another — including the 'natural' volume claimed by opponents. Therefore, the volume produced by rarefaction would be equally natural, so it should persist and not contract. Thus the opponents' argument fails.

Key Terms
القارورة
المص
ضرورة الخلاء
التخلخل والتكاثف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the jar experiment directly proves the existence of vacuum without considering alternative explanations.
Correction: Razi himself presents the rarefaction objection, showing that the proof is not immediately decisive; it requires refuting the alternative.

Checkpoint
According to the opponents' objection, why does water rise into the jar after suction?
A) Because the air is completely removed, creating a vacuum.
B) Because the air expands and then contracts when suction stops.
C) Because water is attracted to the glass.
D) Because the jar becomes lighter.

Key Takeaway
The jar experiment provides an empirical basis for the vacuum, but the rarefaction theory offers a rival explanation that must be refuted.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a seemingly straightforward proof, do you automatically accept it or do you push yourself to consider possible counterarguments, as Razi does? How can you cultivate a similar intellectual honesty in your own faith?
?
The opponents offered a rational alternative to Razi's vacuum proof. Have you ever clung to a comfortable explanation rather than accepting a more challenging truth because it was easier? How will you ensure that your theological beliefs are grounded in truth, not convenience?
?
This lesson demonstrates that even physical observations require logical scrutiny. In what area of your life are you most vulnerable to accepting 'obvious' proofs without questioning deeper assumptions? What one step will you take this week to test a certainty you hold?

Refuting Rarefaction: Foundational Impossibility
Razi gives the first refutation: rarefaction is already proven false.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's first refutation of the rarefaction theory: it has already been proven false.

Core Idea
Rarefaction is already ruled out from earlier arguments.

Having presented the objection based on rarefaction, Razi begins his refutation by appealing to prior established conclusions. The first refutation is concise: the theory of rarefaction and condensation has been demonstrated to be false in previous discussions. In this lesson, we examine the significance of this appeal and the context of that earlier proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the first refutation
Read the single sentence: 'The first: The statement about rarefaction and condensation is invalid and impossible according to what we established.'
2
Understand the reference
Recognize that Razi refers to earlier arguments where rarefaction was refuted.
This may refer to discussions in earlier volumes.
3
Appreciate the strategy
Note that Razi does not repeat the proof here; he relies on established knowledge.
This shows the cumulative nature of kalam arguments.

Why does Razi consider the first refutation sufficient to dismiss the rarefaction objection?

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Causality and Created Things
intermediate
6 min
The Absurdity of Originating Essences
Razi argues that rarefaction would require new essences, leading to absurdity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why rarefaction, even if possible, leads to the absurdity of originating new essences arbitrarily.

Core Idea
Rarefaction would create new essences, which cannot arbitrarily disappear.

Razi's second refutation dives deeper: even if rarefaction were possible, it would require that each expanded part be a new essence (dhat) existing by itself. When the coercer ceases, if some parts vanish while others remain, that is arbitrary discrimination among identical essences. This leads to an absurd conclusion: either all parts perish (impossible) or all remain, meaning the jar stays full and water does not rise. In this lesson, we unpack this intricate argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the second refutation
Read from 'والثاني : هب أن ذلك ممكن' to the end of that section.
2
Identify the key claim
Razi claims that each expanded part is a new essence, not just an attribute.
This is the crucial step.
3
Analyze the impossibility
Understand why it is impossible for some identical parts to cease while others remain.
The principle of indiscernibles leads to an all-or-nothing scenario.
4
Draw the conclusion
Conclude that either nothing vanishes (so jar stays full) or everything vanishes (impossible).
Thus, the rarefaction explanation fails.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة : إن القارورة قد تمص ، ثم تكب على الماء ، فيتصاعد الماء إليها ، ولو كانت بعد المص مملوءة كما كانت قبل ذلك المص ، لوجب أن لا يتصاعد الماء إليها بعد المص ، كما لا يتصاعد الماء إليها قبل المص . فإن قالوا : إن بسبب المص خرج بعض ما كان في القارورة من الهواء ، ثم ازداد حجم البقية ازدياداً امتلات القارورة منه، إلا أن ذلك الازدياد كان قسرياً ، حاصلاً بسبب المص ، فلما كبت القارورة على الماء ، زال القاسر فعاد ذلك الهواء إلى مقداره الطبيعي ، الذي كان حاصلاً أولاً فتصاعد الماء إلى داخل القارورة ، لأجل ضرورة الخلاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think rarefaction only changes volume without creating new substances.
Correction: Razi argues that a change in magnitude implies new parts, each a distinct essence.

Checkpoint
According to Razi's second refutation, what would happen if rarefaction occurred and then the coercer ceased?
A) All parts would vanish.
B) Some parts would vanish arbitrarily.
C) All parts would remain.
D) The air would change color.

Key Takeaway
Razi's second refutation shows that rarefaction leads to an absurd dilemma regarding the persistence of essences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever accepted a plausible explanation for a natural phenomenon without thinking through its deeper implications, as the opponents did with rarefaction? What might be the consequences of such intellectual laziness in your own understanding of Allah's creation? Will you commit to examining your assumptions more carefully?
?
Razi's argument reveals that what seems simple (air rarefying) actually leads to an absurd dilemma if followed logically. Is there an area of your faith or practice where you rely on simplistic reasoning that you have not rigorously tested? What would it take for you to face that discomfort and seek deeper understanding?
?
The dilemma Razi presents forces a choice between two impossible outcomes. In your own life, are there beliefs or habits that create practical contradictions—things you hold onto that lead to inconsistency? What would genuine intellectual honesty require you to abandon or change?

Prime Matter: No Natural Magnitude
Razi uses Ibn Sina's concept of prime matter to refute the rarefaction argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Sina's concept of prime matter undermines the distinction between natural and forced magnitudes.

Core Idea
Prime matter has no inherent magnitude, so no volume is 'natural'.

In his third refutation, Razi invokes Ibn Sina's (the 'Chief Master') view that prime matter (hayula) in itself has no volume or magnitude; it is equally disposed to all magnitudes. This eliminates the opponents' distinction between a 'natural' volume and a 'forced' volume. If all magnitudes are equally related to matter, then the volume produced by rarefaction is as natural as any other. Thus, it cannot revert to a smaller 'natural' volume. In this lesson, we explore this refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the third refutation
Read from 'والوجه الثالث' to the end.
2
Understand prime matter
Ibn Sina's concept: prime matter has no inherent size.
3
Apply equality of relation
If matter relates equally to all magnitudes, then no magnitude is natural vs forced.
4
Draw the consequence
Then the rarefied volume would be natural and should persist, preventing water entry.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة : إن القارورة قد تمص ، ثم تكب على الماء ، فيتصاعد الماء إليها ، ولو كانت بعد المص مملوءة كما كانت قبل ذلك المص ، لوجب أن لا يتصاعد الماء إليها بعد المص ، كما لا يتصاعد الماء إليها قبل المص . فإن قالوا : إن بسبب المص خرج بعض ما كان في القارورة من الهواء ، ثم ازداد حجم البقية ازدياداً امتلات القارورة منه، إلا أن ذلك الازدياد كان قسرياً ، حاصلاً بسبب المص ، فلما كبت القارورة على الماء ، زال القاسر فعاد ذلك الهواء إلى مقداره الطبيعي ، الذي كان حاصلاً أولاً فتصاعد الماء إلى داخل القارورة ، لأجل ضرورة الخلاء
قلنا هذا باطل من وجوه :
الأول : إن القول بالتخلخل والتكاثف باطل محال على ما قررناه .
والثاني : هب أن ذلك ممكن إلا أنا نقول : إن عند حصول هذا التخلخل لزم القول بحدوث الذات، وليس هذا عبارة عن حدوث الصفة فقط لأن الجسم إذا ازداد حجمه ومقداره . فكل جزء من أجزاء ذلك المنبسط المتخلخل فهو ذات قائمة بالنفس كسائر الأجزاء . وأيضاً : فجميع تلك الأجزاء المفترضة في ذلك الجسم متشابهة بالماهية والطبيعة والحقيقة ، فعند زوال القاسر ، أو التقلص والقبض كان ذلك إشارة إلى عدم بعض تلك الأجزاء دون البعض. وهذا باطل . لأن تلك الأجزاء لما كانت متساوية في تمام الماهية لم يكن عدم بعضها أولى من عدم الباقي فإما أن يفنى الكل وهو محال ، أو يبقى الكل ، وحينئذ يلزم أن تبقى القارورة مملوءة كما كانت وحينئذ يجب أن لا يتصاعد الماء إليها بعد المص كما كان لا يتصاعد الماء إليها قبل المص .
والوجه الثالث في دفع هذا السؤال : أن نقول : ذكر الشيخ الرئيس أن الهيولى ليس لها في حد ذاتها وحقيقتها : حجمية ولا مقدار فكانت نسبتها إلى جميع المقادير على السوية ، هذا كلامه
ونحن نقول : إذا كان الأمر كذلك امتنع أن يقال : إن بعض المقادير بالنسبة إلى تلك المادة ، طبيعي لها ، وبعضها قسرى لها . لأن نسبة جميع إليها على السوية . وإذا كان الأمر كذلك ، فهذه الحجمية الحاصلة عند المص وعند التخلخل تكون طبيعة لتلك المادة ، فوجب أن تبقى وأن لا تنتقص عند إكباب القارورة على الماء [ والله أعلم ]
The sixth proof: The jar is sucked, then inverted over water, and the water ascends into it. And if after sucking it were as full as it was before that sucking, then water would not ascend into it after sucking, just as water does not ascend into it before sucking. And if they say: 'Because of the sucking, some of the air that was in the jar exited, then the remainder increased in volume such that the jar became filled with it, except that this increase was forced, occurring due to the sucking; then when the jar was inverted over the water, the coercer ceased and that air returned to its natural quantity that existed initially, so the water ascended into the jar due to the necessity of the vacuum.' We say: This is invalid from several aspects: First: The statement about rarefaction and condensation is invalid and impossible according to what we established. Second: Suppose that is possible, but we say: When this rarefaction occurs, it necessitates the statement of the origination of the essence, and this is not the origination of the attribute alone, because when a body increases in its volume and magnitude, every part of that expanded rarefied part is an essence subsisting in itself like the other parts. Also, all those hypothetical parts in that body are similar in essence, nature, and reality; so when the coercer ceases, or contraction and constriction occur, that would indicate the non-existence of some of those parts without others. And this is invalid because those parts, since they are equal in complete essence, the non-existence of some is no more appropriate than the non-existence of the rest. So either the whole perishes, which is impossible, or the whole remains, and then it follows that the jar remains full as it was, and then water should not ascend into it after sucking just as water did not ascend into it before sucking. The third aspect in repelling this question: We say: The Chief Master (Ibn Sina) mentioned that prime matter has in its own essence and reality neither volume nor magnitude, so its relation to all magnitudes is equal. This is his statement. And we say: If the matter is so, it is impossible to say that some magnitudes are natural for that matter and others are forced for it, because the relation of all of them to it is equal. And if the matter is so, then this volume that occurs during sucking and rarefaction would be natural for that matter, so it must remain and not decrease when the jar is inverted over water. [And God knows best].
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is a full argumentative unit: Razi presents the sixth proof (the jar experiment), then considers an objection from opponents who invoke rarefaction, and refutes it through three distinct aspects.

The proof: When a jar is sucked and then inverted into water, water rises inside. If the jar were still full of air after sucking, water would not rise. Therefore, sucking must have removed some air, creating a vacuum that draws water.

The opponents' objection: They claim that sucking caused some air to leave, but the remaining air expanded (rarefied) to fill the jar; this expansion is forced. When the jar is placed on water, the coercing cause (suction) ceases, so the air contracts back to its natural volume, allowing water to enter to fill the space left by contraction — not a vacuum.

Razi's refutation in three aspects:

First aspect: The theory of rarefaction and condensation has already been proven false in earlier discussions.

Second aspect: Even if rarefaction were possible, it would involve the origination of new essences (not just attributes). Because if air expands, each new portion of expanded volume is a new substance (essence) subsisting by itself, like other parts. And all parts are identical in essence. When the coercer ceases, if some parts vanish while others remain, this would be arbitrary discrimination among identical essences, which is impossible. Therefore, either all parts perish (impossible) or all remain, meaning the jar stays full and water cannot rise.

Third aspect: Citing Ibn Sina (the 'Chief Master'), prime matter (hayula) in itself has no inherent volume or magnitude; it is equally related to all magnitudes. If so, no magnitude is 'natural' to it over another — including the 'natural' volume claimed by opponents. Therefore, the volume produced by rarefaction would be equally natural, so it should persist and not contract. Thus the opponents' argument fails.

Key Terms
الهيولى
المقادير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Razi argue that the expanded volume must remain after the coercer ceases?
A) Because prime matter cannot change.
B) Because prime matter has no natural magnitude, so the expanded volume is as natural as any.
C) Because the jar is sealed.
D) Because Ibn Sina said so.

Key Takeaway
The concept of prime matter with no intrinsic magnitude undermines the notion of a 'natural' volume, thereby refuting the rarefaction explanation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If prime matter has no fixed volume, what does that tell you about your own attachment to physical sizes and shapes? Are you treating temporary forms as if they were permanent essentials?
?
Razi used Ibn Sina's own premise to overturn the rarefaction argument. In your own disagreements, are you willing to meet others on their ground to guide them to truth, or do you insist on your own starting point?
?
This lesson shows that what seems 'natural' can be just a relative equilibrium. Think of a habit you consider 'natural'—could it be that it's merely familiar, not intrinsic? What would it mean to loosen your attachment to it?
