The Argument on Rarefaction and Essence Temporality
An argument that rarefaction implies temporality of essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why rarefaction is argued to necessitate the temporality of the essence itself, not just the attribute.

Core Idea
Rarefaction forces a choice: either all parts vanish or none do.

In this passage, the author presents a philosophical argument linking rarefaction—the expansion of a body—to the temporality of its essence. The argument works through the identity of parts and the impossibility of arbitrary annihilation. This reasoning sets up a problem that the 'third direction' will later resolve.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening claim
Read the first few lines of the Arabic passage: 'التخلخل لزم القول بحدوث الذات'. Understand that rarefaction is being linked to the essence, not just the attribute.
The word 'ذات' (essence) is crucial.
2
Analyze the dilemma
Notice the argument that all parts are identical in quiddity. Upon removal of the compeller, either all parts perish (impossible) or none do, which contradicts observation. Work through this logical case.
The dilemma is based on the principle of sufficient reason.
3
Understand the conclusion
The passage concludes that rarefaction must involve the generation of new essence, implying its temporality. This sets up the need for a response.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التخلخل لزم القول بحدوث الذات، وليس هذا عبارة عن حدوث الصفة فقط لأن الجسم إذا ازداد حجمه ومقداره. فكل جزء من أجزاء ذلك المنبسط المتخلخل فهو ذات قائمة بالنفس كسائر الأجزاء. وأيضاً: فجميع تلك الأجزاء المفترضة في ذلك الجسم متشابهة بالماهية والطبيعة والحقيقة، فعند زوال القاسر، أو التقلص والقبض كان ذلك إشارة إلى عدم بعض تلك الأجزاء دون البعض. وهذا باطل. لأن تلك الأجزاء لما كانت متساوية في تمام الماهية لم يكن عدم بعضها أولى من عدم الباقي فإما أن يفنى الكل وهو محال، أو يبقى الكل، وحينئذ يلزم أن تبقى القارورة مملوءة كما كانت وحينئذ يجب أن لا يتصاعد الماء إليها بعد المص كما كان لا يتصاعد الماء إليها قبل المص. والموجه الثالث في دفع هذا السؤال: أن نقول: ذكر الشيخ الرئيس أن الهيولى ليس لها في حد ذاتها وحقيقتها: حجمية ولا مقدار فكانت نسبتها إلى جميع المقادير على السوية، هذا كلامه. ونحن نقول: إذا كان الأمر كذلك امتنع أن يقال: إن بعض المقادير بالنسبة إلى تلك المادة، طبيعي لها، وبعضها قسرى لها. لأن نسبة جميع إليها على السوية. وإذا كان الأمر كذلك، فهذه الحجمية الحاصلة عند المص وعند التخلخل تكون طبيعة لتلك المادة، فوجب أن تبقى وأن لا تنتقص عند إكباب القارورة على الماء والله أعلم.
Rarefaction necessitates the assertion of the temporality of the essence, and this is not an expression of the temporality of the attribute only, because when a body increases in its volume and magnitude, every part of that expanded, rarefied [body] is a self-subsistent essence like the rest of the parts. Also: all those hypothetical parts in that body are similar in quiddity, nature, and reality; so upon the removal of the compeller, or contraction and constriction, that would indicate the non-existence of some of those parts to the exclusion of others. But this is false, because since those parts are equal in the complete quiddity, the non-existence of some of them is not more preferable than the non-existence of the rest. So either the whole perishes—which is impossible—or the whole remains; and then it would be necessary that the bottle remains full as it was, and then it would be necessary that water does not ascend into it after suction, just as water did not ascend into it before suction. And the third direction in repelling this question is that we say: The Chief Master (Ibn Sina) mentioned that hyle (matter) in its essence and reality has no volume nor magnitude, so its relation to all magnitudes is equal. This is his statement. And we say: If the matter is so, then it is impossible to say that some magnitudes, in relation to that matter, are natural to it and some are compulsory to it, because its relation to all is equal. And if it is so, then this volume that occurs during suction and during rarefaction is natural to that matter; so it must remain and not decrease when the bottle is inverted over water. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage presents an argument about rarefaction and a response to an objection. It begins by stating the consequence of rarefaction: it is claimed that rarefaction necessitates the temporality of the essence, not just the attribute. The author explains that when a body expands, each part is a self-subsistent essence. All parts are identical in quiddity; if some disappear upon removal of a compeller, it is arbitrary and impossible. Therefore, either all perish (impossible) or all remain, which contradicts the observed ascent of water. The third direction (الموجه الثالث) then refutes this by citing Ibn Sina: hyle has no inherent volume, so all volumes are equally related to it. Thus the volume acquired during rarefaction is natural to that matter and must persist. This argument defends the concept of void or rarefaction by appealing to the nature of matter.

Key Terms
تخلخل
ماهية
قاسر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Rarefaction only changes the size as an attribute, without affecting the essence.
Correction: The argument shows that rarefaction necessitates the generation of new essences (parts), so the essence itself is temporal.

Checkpoint
According to the argument, what must happen if rarefaction does not involve the annihilation of parts?
A) The bottle remains full.
B) Water ascends smoothly.
C) The compeller remains.
D) The parts become dissimilar.

Key Takeaway
Rarefaction, if understood as mere expansion without new parts, leads to an impossible arbitrariness; thus it must involve the origination of the essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your own character and habits, do you believe that the core 'you' remains unchanged while only your attributes shift? This lesson argues that even the essence is temporal. How does that challenge your sense of a fixed identity? Will you let Allah reshape your very essence today?
?
The argument says that because parts are identical, it would be arbitrary for some to vanish and others remain. Think about a time you assumed that one sin or flaw was just a surface issue while the rest of you remained 'sound.' Is there a part of your soul you have been treating as permanent that actually needs to be renewed? What step will you take to let that part be recreated by Allah?
?
The bottle analogy reveals that if no new parts are added, the water cannot ascend. Reflect: What 'water'—such as sincere worship, love for Allah, or beneficial knowledge—is failing to rise in your life? Could it be that you are clinging to the old parts of yourself, refusing the new parts Allah wants to create in you through trials or repentance? Will you ask Allah to grant you spiritual expansion?

The Third Direction: Ibn Sina on Hyle and Volume
Ibn Sina's view on hyle used to refute an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn Sina's argument that hyle has no inherent volume, and how that answers objections about rarefaction.

Core Idea
Hyle has no intrinsic magnitude, so any volume it acquires is natural.

After presenting the dilemma of rarefaction, the author turns to the 'third direction'—a response attributed to Ibn Sina. The argument centers on the nature of prime matter (hyle). Ibn Sina claimed that hyle has no volume in itself, so all magnitudes are equally related to it. This implies that the volume acquired during rarefaction is natural and must persist.

Guided Path
1
Read Ibn Sina's claim
Read the part: 'ذكر الشيخ الرئيس أن الهيولى ليس لها في حد ذاتها وحقيقتها: حجمية ولا مقدار'. Understand that hyle in its essence has no volume or magnitude.
'الهيولى' is prime matter.
2
Follow the inference
Since hyle is neutral to all magnitudes, no magnitude can be called natural or compulsory; thus the volume from rarefaction is natural and must remain.
3
Apply to the objection
This refutes the earlier objection about water not ascending, because the volume persists naturally.

Source Text

?

What would it take for you to treat every action as natural to your created potential?
?
Ibn Sina argues that if matter is indifferent, then the volume produced is natural and must remain. Consider your own heart: when you undergo pressures (like suction or rarefaction), do you assume the resulting state is temporary or forced? Or can you trust that even your trials produce a 'natural' state that should persist — not to be escaped, but to be embraced as part of your growth? What would change in your prayer today if you believed that the state you are in right now is exactly where you are meant to be?
?
The passage rejects the idea that some magnitudes are natural and some compulsory. Think of a sin or virtue you consider 'natural' for you. Are you using that label to avoid the work of change? If your nature is truly neutral, then you are free to adopt any 'magnitude' of righteousness. Which limited self-image have you been clinging to, and are you ready to let it go and be shaped by something greater?

Seventh Proof: The Sealed Copper Vessel
Enumerates three possible explanations for water volume increase and refutes two to prove void.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the physical experiment of a sealed copper vessel splitting when heated serves as a proof for the existence of void (al-khala').

Core Idea
The splitting vessel proves void because only empty gaps inside the water can explain the volume increase.

The seventh proof for the existence of void is a physical experiment. The author describes a sealed copper vessel filled with water and heated until it splits. By analyzing the possible causes of the water's volume increase, he eliminates external addition and intrinsic expansion, leaving only the occurrence of internal voids. This lesson guides you through the logical steps of this proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the clear structure: experiment description, three divisions, refutations, and conclusion.
2
Identify the three divisions
The passage presents three possible explanations for the increase in water volume: addition of external matter, intrinsic expansion, and occurrence of internal voids. Find these in the text.
These are the three possibilities listed after 'إما أن يكون'.
3
Understand the refutations
Examine why the first two possibilities are rejected. For the first, note the logical dilemma: if space existed, no splitting; if no space, no entry. For the second, recall previous refutation of self-expansion.
The refutation of the second possibility references earlier reasoning.
4
Conclude with the third
Since only the third possibility remains, the occurrence of empty gaps (voids) is established as the cause of splitting, proving the existence of void.
This is the desired conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السابعة: إن الآنية الصلبة النحاسية إذا أملئت من الماء، ثم سد رأسها سداً وثيقاً، ثم سخنت بالنار القوية فإنها تنشق. وما ذاك إلا أنه ازداد حجم ذلك الماء، فلم يتسع داخل ذلك الإناء له فانشقت الآنية. ونقول: ذلك الازدياد إما أن يكون لأجل أنه نقد فيه شيء من الخارج وانضاف إلى ما كان فيه فصار المجموع زائداً، أو يقال: إنه لم ينضم إليه من الخارج بل صار حجمه ومقداره أزيد مما كان، أو يقال: إنه وقعت الفرج والخلاءات في داخله، فصار حجم المجموع بهذا السبب أزيد مما كان. والقسمان الأولان باطلان، فبقي الثالث وهو المطلوب. أما القسم الأول وهو أنه نقد فيه من الخارج جسم آخر، فهذا لا يوجب الانشقاق. وذلك لأن داخل الأنية إن كان متسعاً لتلك الزيادة، فحينئذ لا يلزم الانشقاق، وإن لم يكن متسعاً لتلك الزيادة فحينئذ لا يحصل النفود البتة، وإذا لم يحصل النفود لم يحصل الانشقاق. وأما القسم الثاني وهو القول بازدياد الحجم، فهو باطل كما سبق تقريره فيما تقدم. ولما فسد هذان القسمان بقي الثالث. وهو أنه إنما حصل الانشقاق، لأنه وقعت الفرج الخالية في داخل ذلك الماء، فصار حجم ذلك المجموع بهذا السبب أزيد مما كان. وذلك يوجب القول بالخلاء.
The seventh proof: A solid copper vessel, if filled with water, then its mouth is tightly sealed, then heated with strong fire, it splits. That is only because the volume of that water increased, and the inside of that vessel did not accommodate it, so the vessel split. And we say: That increase is either because something entered it from outside and was added to what was in it, so the total became greater; or it is said that nothing was added to it from outside, but its volume and magnitude became greater than it was; or it is said that gaps and voids occurred within it, so the volume of the total became greater than it was for this reason. The first two divisions are false, so the third remains—and it is what is sought. As for the first division—that another body entered it from outside—this does not necessitate splitting, because if the inside of the vessel was spacious enough for that increase, then splitting does not occur, and if it was not spacious enough for that increase, then penetration does not occur at all, and if penetration does not occur, splitting does not occur. As for the second division—the claim of increase in volume—it is false as previously established. Since these two divisions are invalid, the third remains: that splitting occurred only because empty gaps occurred inside that water, so the volume of that total became greater than it was for this reason. And that necessitates the affirmation of void.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the existence of void (al-khala'). The author presents an experiment: a solid copper vessel is filled with water, sealed tightly, and heated with strong fire. The vessel splits because the volume of water increases. The author then analyzes the possible causes for the increase in volume: (1) addition of external matter, (2) increase in volume without addition, or (3) occurrence of internal voids. The first is eliminated because if the vessel had space, it would not split; if it had no space, no addition could enter. The second is eliminated as previously refuted. Therefore, the only remaining explanation is the occurrence of empty gaps (voids) within the water, causing the total volume to increase and the vessel to split. This proves the existence of void.

آنية
الزيادة
انشقاق
فرج خالية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The splitting is due to the water's own expansion without voids.
Correction: The author argues that such expansion without addition of matter is impossible based on prior reasoning, so voids must occur.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject the first possibility (addition of matter from outside) for the increase in water volume?
A) Because the vessel is sealed and nothing can enter.
B) Because if the vessel had space, no splitting would occur.
C) Because the water expands uniformly.
D) Because the fire prevents entry.

Key Takeaway
The increase in water volume inside a sealed vessel upon heating can only be explained by the presence of empty gaps (voids) within the water, thereby proving the existence of void.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The proof requires you to accept that empty gaps exist inside the water. In your own understanding of your soul, do you acknowledge that there are 'empty gaps' — areas of ignorance, deficiency, or unmet need? How does the existence of these voids affect your reliance on Allah?
?
The author refutes the idea that external addition caused the volume increase by showing it cannot lead to splitting. Can you identify a time when you attributed a change in your life to an external cause (a person, event, or object) when really the cause was internal — a void within yourself that needed filling? What would it mean to honestly confront that void?

The Eighth Proof: The Narrow-Necked Bottle Experiment
Describes an experiment with a narrow-necked bottle to demonstrate void.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the experiment with a narrow-necked bottle and compressed air suggests the existence of void, and recognize the logical structure of the proof despite its incompleteness.

Core Idea
Compressed air expanding implies void existed within the bottle.

This lesson presents the eighth proof for the existence of void, based on a simple physical experiment. A narrow-necked bottle is blown into, then sealed. When the thumb is removed underwater, bubbles appear, showing that the compressed air expands. This expansion points to the prior existence of void. Although the passage ends abruptly, the intended conclusion is clear.

Guided Path
1
Read the experiment carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Visualize each step: blowing, sealing, immersing, releasing the thumb.
The passage is cut off at the end; focus on the sequence described.
2
Identify the key actions
Note the actions: taking a narrow-necked bottle, blowing into it, placing the thumb on the mouth, immersing in water, removing the thumb.
The thumb prevents air from escaping before the bottle is underwater.
3
Understand the observation
When the thumb is removed underwater, bubbles and air pockets appear. This indicates that the compressed air expands.
Expansion implies there was empty space (void) for the compressed air to fill.
4
Infer the intended conclusion
The author intended to argue that the expansion of compressed air is evidence that void exists inside the bottle before the thumb is removed.
Even though the proof is incomplete, the reasoning is recoverable.

Source Text

Then when we immerse it in water and remove the thumb from its mouth, bubbles and air pockets appear in the water. That is because the air which we introduced into [it] is intensely...
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage begins an eighth proof for the existence of void. It describes an experiment: a narrow-necked bottle is blown into, the mouth is quickly sealed with the thumb to prevent air escape, then the bottle is immersed in water. When the thumb is removed, bubbles appear in the water. The author explains that this is because the air introduced into the bottle was intensely [compressed?]. The argument is cut off, but the intention is to show that the compressed air expands when released, implying the existence of void. The proof is incomplete due to the page ending.

The expansion of compressed air when released indicates that void existed inside the bottle before the thumb was removed.

?

?

?

Are you ready to let a straightforward truth upend a comfortable assumption you hold—about the world, about yourself, or about God? What will you do with that truth before you close this lesson?

The Brass Vessel Experiment: Proving Void by Elimination
Razi proves void by logical elimination from a heat experiment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the brass vessel experiment demonstrates the existence of void (al-khala') through logical elimination of alternatives.

Core Idea
An observed effect forces us to accept what reason says must be there.

This lesson presents one of the most ingenious proofs for the existence of void — the brass vessel experiment. By heating a sealed water-filled vessel until it bursts, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi argues that the only explanation for the increased volume is the formation of empty gaps inside the water. This argument illustrates how kalam uses empirical observations together with logical analysis to establish metaphysical truths.

Guided Path
1
Understand the experimental setup
Read the description of the experiment: a solid brass vessel filled with water, tightly sealed, then heated with strong fire until it splits.
The splitting is the empirical observation that needs explanation.
2
Identify the three possible explanations
The author lists three possible causes for the increase in volume: (1) external matter entering, (2) the water's volume increasing without addition, (3) formation of voids inside the water.
These three options are exhaustive and mutually exclusive.
3
Follow the elimination of the first explanation
The first possibility (external matter entering) is dismissed because if the vessel had space for extra matter, no splitting would occur; if it lacked space, nothing could enter.
4
Follow the elimination of the second explanation
The second possibility (volume increase without addition) is rejected as previously refuted in earlier proofs.
This refers to the idea of volume increase without new atoms being added.
5
Grasp the conclusion: voids must exist
Only the third possibility remains: empty gaps (voids) form inside the water, increasing its total volume and causing the vessel to split.
This logically establishes the existence of void (al-khala').

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السابعة : إن الآنية الصلبة النحاسية إذا أملئت من الماء ، ثم سد رأسها سداً وثيقاً ، ثم سخنت بالنار القوية فإنها تنشق . وما ذاك إلا أنه أزداد حجم ذلك الماء ، قلم يتسع داخل ذلك الإناء له فانشقت الآنية . ونقول : ذلك الازدياد إما أن يكون لأجل أن نقد فيه شيء من الخارج وانضاف إلى ما كان فيه فصار المجموع زائداً ، أو يقال : إنه لم ينضم إليه من الخارج بل صار حجمه ومقداره أزيد مما كان ، أو يقال : إنه وقعت الفرج والخلاءات في داخله ، فصار حجم المجموع بهذا السبب أزيد مما كان . والقسمان الاولان باطلان ، فبقي الثالث وهو المطلوب. أما القسم الأول وهو أنه نقد فيه من الخارج جسم آخر ، فهذا لا يوجب الانشقاق . وذلك لأن داخل الأنية إن كان متسعاً لتلك الزيادة ، فحينئذ لا يلزم الانشقاق ، وإن لم يكن متسعاً لتلك الزيادة فحينئذ لا يحصل النفود البتة ، وإذا لم يحصل النفود لم يحصل الانشقاق . وأما القسم الثاني وهو القول بازدياد الحجم، فهو باطل كما سبق تقريره فيما تقدم. ولما فسد هذان القسمان بقي الثالث . وهو أنه إنما حصل الانشقاق ، لأنه وقعت الفرج الخالية في داخل ذلك الماء ، فصار حجم ذلك المجموع بهذا السبب أزيد مما كان . وذلك يوجب القول بالخلاء.
The seventh proof: If a solid brass vessel is filled with water, then its opening is tightly sealed, then it is heated with a strong fire, it splits. This is only because the volume of that water increased, so the interior of that vessel did not accommodate it, so the vessel split. We say: That increase is either (1) because something from outside entered and was added to what was in it, so the total became larger; or (2) it is said that nothing from outside was added to it, but rather its volume and magnitude became more than it was; or (3) it is said that gaps and voids occurred in its interior, so the volume of the total due to this reason became more than it was. The first two divisions are false, so the third remains, and it is what is sought. As for the first division—that another body from outside entered into it—this does not necessitate splitting. That is because if the interior of the vessel was spacious enough for that increase, then splitting would not necessarily occur; and if it was not spacious enough for that increase, then entry would not happen at all; and if entry does not happen, splitting does not occur. As for the second division—the claim of increase in volume—it is false as previously established. When these two divisions are invalid, the third remains: namely that splitting occurred only because empty gaps occurred inside that water, so the volume of that total due to this reason became more than it was. That necessitates the affirmation of void.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh proof for the existence of void (al-khala'). The author describes an experiment: a sealed brass vessel filled with water, when heated, bursts. This is attributed to the increase in volume of the water. The author then analyzes the possible explanations for this increase. Three possibilities are considered: (1) external matter enters and adds to the volume; (2) the water's volume increases without any addition of matter; (3) empty gaps (voids) appear within the water, causing the overall volume to increase. The first possibility is rejected because if the vessel had enough space, no bursting would occur, and if it lacked space, no entry is possible. The second possibility (volume increase without addition) is dismissed as previously refuted. Thus the third explanation remains: voids form inside the water, increasing its total volume, which necessitates the existence of void. This argument is a key support for the Ash'ari position that vacuum is possible.

Key Terms
خلاء
آنية
انشقاق
ازدياد حجم
فرج خالية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof merely assumes that voids exist without empirical evidence.
Correction: The proof actually starts from an observed physical event (the vessel splitting) and uses logical elimination of alternative explanations to conclude that voids must be present. It is not an assumption but a necessary conclusion.

Checkpoint
According to the seventh proof, why does the brass vessel split when heated?
A) Because water expands, requiring more space, leading to voids.
B) Because external fire enters the vessel.
C) Because the water condenses.
D) Because the vessel's walls weaken.

Key Takeaway
The brass vessel experiment forces us to accept the existence of void as the only logical explanation for the observed expansion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This proof requires you to accept an unseen reality (void) based on logical elimination. Are there aspects of your faith that you struggle to accept because they are unseen? How can this method of reasoning strengthen your conviction?
?
The vessel bursts because it cannot accommodate the increase. In your life, what blessings or trials have forced you to expand beyond your capacity? Could that 'bursting' point you to a reality you need to embrace?
?
Razi eliminates alternatives until only one remains. Think of a personal belief you hold. Have you honestly considered and eliminated alternative explanations? What would it take to be as rigorous as this proof demands?

The Flask and Bubbles: An Empirical Proof for Void
Razi proves void via a flask experiment with bubbles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses the flask and bubbles experiment to argue for the existence of void, and why the objection based on rarefaction and condensation is considered weak.

Core Idea
A simple flask experiment demonstrates that void must exist, because extra air can be added into a seemingly full space.

In this eighth proof, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi presents a simple but powerful empirical demonstration: by blowing air into a sealed flask and submerging it in water, bubbles appear when the thumb is released. He argues that this shows extra air was introduced, implying the flask contained void spaces. The passage also addresses the counterargument of rarefaction and condensation, which Razi dismisses as already refuted.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully to understand the experimental procedure described.
Notice the precise steps: blowing, sealing, submerging, releasing.
2
Identify the Core Argument
Identify the logical inference: the emergence of bubbles shows extra air was introduced, implying the flask was not completely full initially.
The key is that if the flask were completely full, no additional air could be added.
3
Understand the Objection
Recognize the objection based on rarefaction and condensation (takhalkhul wa takathuf) and note that Razi says it has already been refuted.
Think about why rarefaction might be offered as an alternative explanation.
4
Reflect on the Proof's Significance
Consider how this experiment serves as empirical evidence for the existence of void, and how it fits within the larger theological framework.
This proof relies on direct physical observation rather than pure logic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثامنة : إنا نأخذ قارورة ضيقة الرأس ، وننفخ فيها نفخاً شديداً ، ثم نضع الإبهام بعد قطع النفخ على فمها سريعاً ، لئلا يخرج منها الريح الذي نفخناه فيها ، فإذا غمسناها في الماء وأزلنا الإبهام عن رأسها ، ظهرت في الماء نفاخات وبقابق. وذلك لأن الريح الذي أدخلناه في القارورة بسبب النفخ الشديد ، يخرج عنها، ويشق سطح الماء عند الصعود فلا جرم تظهر النفاخات والبقابق . وذلك يدل على أنا أدخلنا في تلك القارورة عند النفخ من الهواء ، ما لولا النفخ لما دخل فيه ، ولو كانت القارورة مملوءة من الهواء لما أمكن إدخال هواء أزيد فيه . والجواب الذي يذكرونه من حيث التخلخل والتكاثف ، فقد عرفت ضعفه وسقوطه . والله أعلم .
The eighth proof: We take a narrow-necked flask and blow into it with a strong blow, then after stopping the blowing we quickly place the thumb over its mouth, so that the air we blew into it does not escape. Then when we immerse it in water and remove the thumb from its mouth, bubbles and blobs appear in the water. That is because the air that we introduced into the flask due to the strong blowing exits from it and breaks the surface of the water upon rising, so inevitably bubbles and blobs appear. This indicates that we introduced into that flask, at the time of blowing, air that without blowing would not have entered it; and if the flask had been full of air, it would not have been possible to introduce additional air into it. The answer that they mention regarding rarefaction and condensation—you have already known its weakness and invalidity. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage presents the eighth proof for the existence of void. The experiment involves a narrow-necked flask: after blowing air into it, the thumb is placed to seal it, then the flask is submerged in water. When the thumb is removed, bubbles emerge. The author argues that this shows extra air was forced into the flask, implying that the flask was not completely filled with air initially; otherwise, no extra air could have been added. This indicates the presence of void spaces that were filled by the introduced air. The author notes that the objection based on rarefaction and condensation (takhalkhul wa takathuf) is weak and has already been refuted. The argument is a direct empirical demonstration that void exists, as the extra air must occupy previously empty spaces.

Key Terms
قارورة
نفخ
نفاخات
بقابق
تخلخل
تكاثف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The bubbles are due to compressed air expanding when the thumb is released.
Correction: The author's point is that the extra air was introduced by blowing; if the flask were full, no extra air could be added. The bubbles show that the air was already in the flask (trapped) and escapes, proving prior emptiness, not just compression.

Checkpoint
What does the flask experiment demonstrate according to the author?
A) Air can be compressed.
B) The flask originally contained void, allowing extra air to be added.
C) Water vapor enters the flask.
D) The flask's glass is porous.

Key Takeaway
The flask experiment provides empirical evidence for void by showing that additional air can be forced into a container, implying the presence of empty spaces.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Razi shows that a flask seemingly full can still receive more air. Is there an area of your life—such as your understanding, your faith, or your character—where you have assumed you have no room for growth? What would it mean to admit that you have a void that only God's guidance can fill?
?
The philosopher dismisses a counterargument as weak. Have you ever clung to an explanation that you knew was weak because it was comfortable? Before reading this, did you believe that the physical world is completely full and solid? How does recognizing emptiness in the world challenge you to see your own need for the Creator?

Why Rest in the Void is Impossible
Sanusi argues that rest in the void is impossible due to uniformity; objection and refutation follow.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a body cannot be at rest in the void, based on the principle that preponderance without a preponderant factor is impossible.

Core Idea
Rest in the void would require an arbitrary choice, which is impossible.

In this lesson, we examine the second proof against the void. The author argues that if the void existed, a body could not be at rest in it because all parts of the void are identical. The lesson also addresses the objection that God's free will could specify a location.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening claim
Start with the claim that rest in the void is impossible. Notice how the author frames the argument as a conditional.
The claim is part of a larger proof that the void cannot be a place.
2
Examine the reasoning from uniformity
The author explains that the void is either pure non-existence or a uniform extension. In both cases, all parts are identical, so choosing one part for rest would be arbitrary.
This relies on the principle that a choice without a cause is impossible.
3
Consider the objection and its refutation
The objector suggests God's free will can specify a location. The refutation shows that either the location has an attribute (which leads to regress) or not (which is arbitrary).
This demonstrates the depth of the argument, addressing potential counterpoints.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية : إنه لو حصل الخلاء ، لكان كون الجسم ساكناً فيه : محالاً ، ولكان كونه متحركاً فيه : محالاً . ومتى كان الأمر كذلك ، امتنع كون الخلاء مكاناً للجسم. إنما قلنا : إن الخلاء يمتنع كونه مكاناً للجسم المتحرك وللجسم الساكن . وذلك لأن الخلاء إما أن يكون عدماً محضاً ، ونفياً صرفاً ، على ما يقوله المتكلمون . أو يكون بعداً متشابه الأجزاء والجوانب على ما هو قول القدماء من الحكماء. وعلى التقديرين فلا اختلاف بين أجزائه وأبعاضه البتة ، وإذا كان كذلك ، امتنع أن يسكن الجسم في جزء من أجزائه وجانب من جوانبه . لأن الجسم لو بقي مستقراً فيه طالباً له لازماً للبقاء فيه مع كونه مساوياً لسائر الجوانب والأطراف ، يلزم رجحان أحد طرفي الممكن على الآخر لا لمرجح ، وهو محال . فإن قالوا : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : إن الفاعل المختار يخصص ذلك بذلك الحيز المعين بقصده واختياره ؟ فنقول : إن كان ذلك الحيز المعني موصوفا بأمر ، لأجله صار أولى بتخصيص ذلك الجسم به ، عاد الطلب في أن ذلك الحيز ، كيف اختص بذلك المرجح ؟ وإن لم يوجد هذا المرجح ، كان رجحان القصد إلى تخصيص ذلك الجسم به دون سائر الجوانب ترجيحاً للممكن من غير مرجح وأيضاً فيمتنع أن يتحرك الجسم فيه . لأن الحركة عبارة عن ترك حيز ، وطلب حيز آخر . وذلك لا يتم إلا بأن يكون ذلك الحيز مخالفاً لذلك الحيز ، في أمر من الأمور ، وإلا لكان تخصيص أحد الجانبين بالهرب ، والآخر بالطلب ، رجحاناً للممكن من غير مرجح . وهو محال . فثبت : أن بتقدير حصول الخلاء يمتنع كون الجسم ساكناً فيه ، ويمتنع كونه متحركاً
The second proof: If the void existed, then the body being at rest in it would be impossible, and its being in motion in it would be impossible. And whenever the matter is so, the void being a place for the body is impossible. We say: The void is impossible as a place for the moving body and for the stationary body. That is because the void is either pure non-existence and absolute negation, according to what the mutakallimun say, or it is a uniform extension in parts and directions according to what the ancient philosophers say. On both suppositions, there is no difference whatsoever between its parts and segments. And if that is the case, it is impossible for the body to settle in a part of it and a direction of its directions. For if the body were to remain stable in it, seeking it, adhering to staying in it, while it is equal to all other directions and sides, then the preponderance of one of the two sides of the possible over the other without a preponderant factor would be entailed, and that is impossible. If they say: 'Why is it not permissible to say that the free agent (al-fāʿil al-mukhtār) specifies that body to that particular space by His intention and choice?' We say: If that particular space is described with an attribute by which it becomes more worthy of being specified for that body, then the inquiry returns as to how that space was specifically characterized with that preponderant factor. And if this preponderant factor does not exist, then the preponderance of the intention to specify that body to it over all other directions would be a preponderance of the possible without a preponderant factor. And also, it is impossible for the body to move in it. For motion is the leaving of a space and the seeking of another space. That is not completed unless that space is different from that space in some matter; otherwise, specifying one of the two directions for leaving and the other for seeking would be a preponderance of the possible without a preponderant factor, and that is impossible. So it is established that, given the existence of the void, it is impossible for the body to be at rest in it and impossible for it to be in motion in it.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage presents the second argument against the void (khala'). The argument is twofold: first, void cannot serve as a place for a body at rest or in motion. Why? The void is either pure non-existence (as mutakallimun claim) or a uniform extension with no differentiation (as ancient philosophers claim). In both cases, all parts of the void are identical. Therefore, if a body were at rest in a specific part of the void, it would have to prefer that part over others without any distinguishing feature—this leads to the impossibility of preponderance without a preponderant factor (tarjīḥ bilā murajjiḥ). Similarly, for motion: motion requires leaving one space and seeking another, which is only possible if the two spaces differ in some respect; otherwise, the choice of which space to leave and which to seek would again be arbitrary. The text then addresses an objection: Why not attribute the specification to God's free will (al-fāʿil al-mukhtār)? The answer: If the chosen space has some attribute making it worthy, the question regresses; if not, then God's choice itself would be a preponderance without a preponderant factor, which is also impossible. Thus, void cannot be a place for bodies.

Key Terms
خلاء
ساكن
مكان
عدم محض
بعد متشابه
رجحان
مرجح
الفاعل المختار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God's will alone can arbitrarily specify a location in the void, making rest possible.
Correction: The argument shows that even God's will cannot arbitrarily choose without a reason, as that would entail preponderance without a preponderant factor, which is impossible.

Checkpoint
Why does the text argue that rest in the void is impossible?
A) Because the void has no resistance to support rest.
B) Because all parts of the void are identical, making any choice of location arbitrary.
C) Because bodies cannot be at rest in non-existence.
D) Because rest requires a cause, and the void has no cause.

Key Takeaway
Rest in the void is impossible because choosing a location would require an arbitrary preponderance, which is rationally impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are there decisions in your life—big or small—that you make without a real reason, simply because you 'felt like it'? How does this argument against arbitrary preponderance call you to examine the basis of your choices?
?
If God's will is never arbitrary, what does that mean for your trust in His plan, especially when you cannot see the reason behind a trial or blessing? Will you commit to trusting that His choice has a perfect reason, even when hidden?
?
The void argument shows that rest without a cause is impossible. In your spiritual life, are you resting on a 'void'—on a habit or belief you have never truly examined? What one step will you take today to replace that with a well-founded conviction?

Why Motion in the Void is Also Impossible
Sanusi argues that motion in the void is impossible due to uniformity, completing the second proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why motion in the void is impossible, and how the argument completes the proof that void cannot be a place.

Core Idea
Motion requires distinct spaces; in the void, all spaces are identical, making motion impossible.

Having established that rest in the void is impossible, the author now turns to motion. He defines motion as leaving one space and seeking another. In the void, all spaces are uniform, so choosing one space to leave and another to seek would be arbitrary. This completes the proof that the void cannot serve as a place for bodies.

Guided Path
1
Read the motion argument
The author claims that motion in the void is also impossible. He defines motion and explains why the void's uniformity prevents it.
Notice that motion requires two distinct spaces: the one being left and the one being sought.
2
Understand the requirement of difference
For motion to occur, the space left and the space sought must differ in some aspect. Otherwise, the choice of which space to leave and which to seek is arbitrary.
This again relies on the principle of no preponderance without a preponderant factor.
3
See the conclusion
Since both rest and motion are impossible in the void, the void cannot be a place for bodies, thus refuting the belief in void.
This solidifies the second proof against the void.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

intermediate

Second Proof Against Void: Body Cannot Rest or Move in It
Fakhr al-Din al-Razi argues that body cannot be at rest or in motion in a void.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a body cannot be at rest or in motion in a void, and how this leads to the conclusion that void cannot serve as a place for body.

Core Idea
If void existed, rest and motion become impossible due to the absence of distinguishing factors.

Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's second argument against the void is a logical masterpiece: he shows that whether void is absolute nothingness or uniform extension, its parts are indistinguishable. Therefore, a body cannot have a reason to be at rest in one part rather than another, nor can it have a reason to move from one part to another. The argument is reinforced by addressing the objection that a free agent could arbitrarily choose a location. This lesson unpacks the reasoning that ultimately disproves the possibility of void.

Guided Path
1
Read the full argument
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the clear structure: initial claim, analysis of void, argument against rest, argument against motion, objection and response.
Pay attention to the phrase 'tarjīḥ bilā murajjiḥ' — preference without a preponderator.
2
Understand the nature of void
Al-Razi considers two definitions of void: pure nothingness (mutakallimūn) or uniform extension (philosophers). In both cases, void has no internal differences.
This uniformity is key to the argument.
3
Follow the argument against rest
If a body rests in a specific part of void, it must have a reason. Since all parts are identical, there is no reason — so rest is impossible.
This is an application of the principle of sufficient reason.
4
Follow the argument against motion
Motion requires leaving one part for another. If all parts are identical, there is no reason to leave one and seek another. Thus motion is also impossible.
Hence void cannot be a place for either rest or motion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية : إنه لو حصل الخلاء ، لكان كون الجسم ساكناً فيه : محالاً ، ولكان كونه متحركاً فيه : محالاً . ومتى كان الأمر كذلك ، امتنع كون الخلاء مكاناً للجسم. إنما قلنا : إن الخلاء يمتنع كونه مكاناً للجسم المتحرك وللجسم الساكن . وذلك لأن الخلاء إما أن يكون عدماً محضاً ، ونفياً صرفاً، على ما يقوله المتكلمون . أو يكون بعداً متشابه الأجزاء والجوانب على ما هو قول القدماء من الحكماء. وعلى التقديرين فلا اختلاف بين أجزائه وأبعاضه البتة ، وإذا كان كذلك، امتنع أن يسكن الجسم في جزء من أجزائه وجانب من جوانبه . لأن الجسم لو بقي مستقراً فيه طالباً له لازماً للبقاء فيه مع كونه مساوياً لسائر الجوانب والأطراف، يلزم رجحان أحد طرفي الممكن على الآخر لا لمرجح، وهو محال .
فإن قالوا : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : إن الفاعل المختار يخصص ذلك بذلك الحيز المعين بقصده واختياره ؟ فنقول : إن كان ذلك الحيز المعين موصوفاً بأمر، لأجله صار أولى بتخصيص ذلك الجسم به، عاد الطلب في أن ذلك الحيز، كيف اختص بذلك المرجح ؟ وإن لم يوجد هذا المرجح، كان رجحان القصد إلى تخصيص ذلك الجسم به دون سائر الجوانب ترجيحاً للممكن من غير مرجح . وأيضاً فيمتنع أن يتحرك الجسم فيه . لأن الحركة عبارة عن ترك حيز، وطلب حيز آخر . وذلك لا يتم إلا بأن يكون ذلك الحيز مخالفاً لذلك الحيز، في أمر من الأمور، وإلا لكان تخصيص أحد الجانبين بالهرب، والآخر بالطلب، ترجيحاً للممكن من غير مرجح . وهو محال . فثبت : أن بتقدير حصول الخلاء يمتنع كون الجسم ساكناً فيه، ويمتنع كونه متحركاً فيه . وإذا كان كذلك، وجب القطع بأنه يمتنع أن يكون الخلاء مكاناً للجسم . والله أعلم .
The second proof: If void existed, then for a body to be at rest in it would be impossible, and for it to be in motion in it would be impossible. And whenever the matter is thus, void's being a place for body is impossible. We only say: void is impossible as a place for the moving body and for the stationary body. That is because void is either pure non-existence and absolute negation, as the theologians (mutakallimūn) say, or an extension similar in parts and aspects, as is the saying of the ancient philosophers. On both suppositions, there is no difference between its parts and portions at all. And if it is thus, it is impossible for the body to be stationary in a part of its parts and a side of its sides. Because if the body remained settled in it, seeking it, adhering to remaining in it, while it is equal to all other sides and extremities, it would necessitate preference of one of the two possible sides over the other without a preponderator, and that is impossible. If they say: Why is it not permissible to say that the free agent (al-fā‘il al-mukhtār) specifies that body to that specific location by his intention and choice? We say: If that specific location is described with something due to which it becomes more worthy of specifying that body with it, then the inquiry returns as to how that location became distinguished by that preponderator. And if this preponderator does not exist, then the preference of the intention to specify that body with it over all other sides would be a preponderance of the possible without a preponderator. And also, it is impossible for the body to move in it. Because motion is leaving one location and seeking another location. That is not accomplished unless that location is different from that location in some matter; otherwise, specifying one side by fleeing and the other by seeking would be a preponderance of the possible without a preponderator, and that is impossible. So it is established that, given the existence of void, it is impossible for the body to be at rest in it, and it is impossible for it to be in motion in it. And if it is thus, it is necessary to conclude that it is impossible for void to be a place for body. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage presents the second argument against the existence of void (al-khalāʼ). The author, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, begins by stating the conclusion: if void existed, a body could neither be at rest nor in motion in it, so void cannot be a place for body. He then justifies this by analyzing the nature of void. Void, he explains, is either absolute nothingness (as the mutakallimūn hold) or an extension uniform in all parts (as the ancient philosophers hold). In either case, its parts are indistinguishable. Therefore, if a body were at rest in a particular part of void, there would be no reason for it to prefer that part over any other—this would be a preference without a preponderator (tarjīḥ bilā murajjiḥ), which is impossible. Likewise, motion requires that the body leaves one location and seeks another; but if all parts of void are identical, there is no reason to flee one and seek another, again implying preference without cause. The author then anticipates an objection: could not a free agent (God) simply choose a specific location? The response is that if the location has no distinguishing feature, the agent's choice would still be arbitrary preference without a reason. If it does have a distinguishing feature, then that feature becomes the preponderator, and the question shifts to how that feature itself was determined. Thus, the argument stands: void cannot serve as a place, and since a body must be in some place, void cannot exist.

Key Terms
الخلاء
السكون
الحركة
المرجح
الفاعل المختار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's arbitrary choice can determine a body's location in void without a reason.
Correction: The argument shows that even if a free agent chooses, the choice itself would be a preference without a preponderator if the location has no distinguishing feature, which is rationally impossible.

Checkpoint
Why is a body's rest in void considered impossible according to the second argument?
A) Because void does not exist at all.
B) Because if all parts of void are identical, preferring one part for rest would be a preference without a preponderator.
C) Because bodies cannot be at rest in any place.
D) Because the mutakallimūn deny the existence of void.

Key Takeaway
The impossibility of rest and motion in void proves that void cannot serve as a place for body, and thus void cannot exist.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make decisions, do you often rely on arbitrary preferences or do you seek legitimate reasons? How does the argument about 'preference without a preponderator' challenge you to examine the grounds of your choices?
?
The objection suggests that God's arbitrary choice could explain the body's location, but the argument shows even divine will requires a reason. Do you live as if your actions are guided by wisdom or by whim? What would change if you held every decision accountable to a reason?
?
The argument demonstrates that something cannot be a place if it provides no basis for rest or motion. In your own life, are there 'voids'—areas where you expect stability or progress but lack clear reasons? How can you fill those voids with purpose?
